## Gemini-3.1-pro
Here is a comprehensive manuscript review following the requested structure and the rigorous standards expected of a *Nature Communications* reviewer. 

***

### 1. Summary
[cite_start]The manuscript presents a profile-driven, behavioral simulation framework designed to evaluate organic optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory (CIM) systems for edge vision tasks[cite: 8]. [cite_start]By mapping literature-derived and proxy device characteristics (such as conductance states, noise, and retention) to neural network performance (ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M), the study identifies system-level deployment bottlenecks[cite: 9, 29]. [cite_start]The core claim is that standard quantization and standard stochastic noise are not the primary limits for modern architectures; rather, ADC precision, task complexity, cross-device mismatch, and non-linear write dynamics dictate viability[cite: 10, 11].

### 2. Significance & Novelty
* [cite_start]**Gap Addressed:** The work effectively targets the persistent "decision gap" between isolated materials characterization (which often stops at toy network validation) and system-level CIM simulators (which are largely tailored to mature, inorganic electrical non-volatile memories)[cite: 21, 24, 26]. 
* **Contribution Type:** The contribution is strictly methodological and analytical. [cite_start]It introduces a transparent, Python-based bridge for evaluating optoelectronic frontends and hybrid analog/digital operators[cite: 28, 38, 64]. 
* [cite_start]**Comparison to SOTA Tools:** The author rightly points out that while tools like DNN+NeuroSim and AIHWKIT are foundational, they are not natively organized around optical frontend transduction or organic profile-substitution[cite: 63, 64]. 
* **Venue Fit:** As a purely simulation-based study lacking new physical device fabrication, it faces a high barrier for *Nature Communications*. The analytical insights—particularly the failure modes of Vision Transformers under proportional noise and the inverse-gamma shot-noise amplification—are strong, but the paper might be better suited for a top-tier methodology/device-modeling journal (e.g., *Nature Electronics* or IEEE TCAD) unless the author can definitively prove that this framework reveals physical phenomena that existing inorganic simulators fundamentally obscure.

### 3. Technical Soundness
* [cite_start]**Physical Assumptions:** The behavioral approximations are clearly stated, particularly the omission of IR drop, sneak paths, and dedicated interconnect routing[cite: 574, 576]. While acceptable for a "first-order" model, these omissions heavily favor the analog crossbar's energy metrics. 
* [cite_start]**Device-to-System Mapping:** The differential conductance mapping coupled with digital scale recovery is standard[cite: 148, 151]. [cite_start]However, relying on "ideal calibrated digital post-processing" for scale recovery without rigorously penalizing its digital energy cost may skew the 11.45x efficiency claim[cite: 152, 515].
* [cite_start]**Controls & Statistics:** Excellent use of multi-run Monte Carlo evaluations for inference stochasticity[cite: 202]. [cite_start]The inclusion of standard FP32 baselines provides necessary grounding[cite: 212].
* [cite_start]**Potential Issues:** * *ADC Modeling:* The sharp 6-bit cliff observed for Tiny-ViT is highly interesting, but it is unclear if this is a fundamental ViT limitation or an artifact of the specific attention-mapping heuristic[cite: 371, 372]. 
    * [cite_start]*Retention:* The author uses a uniform double-exponential decay model for the canonical tests[cite: 159, 429]. [cite_start]Given that organic materials often suffer from severe state-dependent drift, relegating the state-dependent evaluation to a supplementary sanity check weakens the robustness claims[cite: 430, 431].

### 4. Presentation & Narrative
* **Story Arc:** The narrative is exceptionally well-structured. [cite_start]Organizing the introduction around four specific, deployment-facing questions creates a strong roadmap[cite: 31, 32, 33, 34]. 
* [cite_start]**Abstract:** Accurately and concisely reflects the core methodology, the datasets, and the most critical findings[cite: 8, 9, 10, 11].
* **Figures:** The figures are clean and publication-quality. [cite_start]However, Figure 10 (Attention Heatmaps) is purely qualitative[cite: 684]. In a rigorous evaluation, these visual maps should be accompanied by a quantitative similarity metric (e.g., structural similarity or attention entropy) to mathematically justify the distortion claims.
* [cite_start]**Self-Awareness:** Section 6.6 (Limitations) is candid and thorough, which builds immense trust with the reader[cite: 570, 571].

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons
* [cite_start]**AIHWKIT Extensibility:** The author states that running identical workloads through IBM's AIHWKIT falls outside the scope[cite: 567]. As a Reviewer, I disagree. Because AIHWKIT is highly extensible and allows for custom noise and drift injection, the author *must* provide a baseline comparison to prove that their custom framework provides capabilities (or execution efficiencies) that a custom-configured AIHWKIT pipeline cannot.
* **ViT Quantization Literature:** The discussion on the 6-bit ViT cliff would benefit from citing recent ML literature on post-training quantization (PTQ) for Vision Transformers, as the ML community has already identified softmax and attention products as highly sensitive to low-bitwidth bottlenecks.

### 6. Specific Issues
* [cite_start]**Speculative Claims:** In Section 6.3, the failure of the model on the Flowers-102 dataset is attributed to a "HAT Data-Floor Hypothesis," suggesting stochastic hardware noise regularizes the model too aggressively on small datasets[cite: 554, 556]. This is highly speculative. The author needs to provide a data-ablation study (e.g., artificially reducing CIFAR-10) to isolate data volume from domain-shift before introducing this hypothesis.
* [cite_start]**Energy Overhead:** Section 5.10 notes a 273.94 $\mu$J inference cost, but Section 6.6 admits interconnect data marshaling is not itemized[cite: 515, 574]. The energy claims should include a sensitivity sweep showing how the 11.45x advantage degrades if routing/marshaling costs scale up.
* [cite_start]**Ensemble HAT Realism:** Ensemble HAT effectively solves cross-device mismatch algorithmically by resampling D2D masks per epoch[cite: 504, 505]. However, in physical deployment, an edge device is flashed *once* to a specific, static array. The manuscript must clarify how a model trained on rapidly shifting simulated arrays successfully maps to a static physical array without instance-specific calibration.

### 7. Questions for Authors
1.  Can you provide a simple data-ablation study (e.g., training on 10%, 25%, and 50% of CIFAR-10) to empirically validate the "HAT Data-Floor Hypothesis" observed on the Flowers-102 dataset?
2.  In your energy model, how is the "digital scale recovery" physically implemented, and does the lack of accounting for the digital multipliers required for this step artificially inflate the hybrid analog energy advantage?
3.  Given that AIHWKIT allows for custom drift, noise, and clipping modules, what specific organic optoelectronic behaviors (besides the optical frontend) are fundamentally impossible to simulate in AIHWKIT, thereby strictly necessitating this new framework?
4.  For Figure 10, can you replace or supplement the visual heatmaps with a quantitative metric measuring the divergence of the attention distributions between the FP32 baseline and the noisy models?

### 8. Overall Recommendation
**Major Revision.** *Justification:* The manuscript is beautifully written, logically structured, and provides highly valuable insights into the architecture-specific vulnerabilities of CNNs versus ViTs on organic CIM hardware. However, it requires a major revision to meet the empirical standards of *Nature Communications*. Specifically, the paper relies on speculative hypotheses for its dataset-scaling failures, lacks a head-to-head control comparison against existing extensible simulators (like AIHWKIT) to prove the necessity of the tool, and relies on qualitative visual evidence for attention map distortions. Tightening the energy accounting and providing ablation studies for the data-floor hypothesis will significantly strengthen the manuscript's physical and algorithmic claims.

## Perplexity Sonar

I now have comprehensive access to the full manuscript. Let me provide a thorough review.

***

# Reviewer #2 Report — *Nature Communications*

**Manuscript:** "Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision"
**Author:** Songqiao Li
**Submitted:** April 9, 2026

***

## 1. Summary

This manuscript presents a profile-driven, first-order behavioral simulation framework for evaluating organic optoelectronic synaptic transistors in compute-in-memory (CIM) inference for edge vision tasks. The framework maps literature-derived or measured device parameters — conductance windows, variability, retention, ADC precision, and optical front-end distortion — into task-level accuracy and energy estimates across ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M on CIFAR-10, CIFAR-100, and Flowers-102. The central claim is that quantization is *not* the dominant bottleneck; instead, ADC precision, hardware-instance variability, and nonlinear write dynamics are more critical deployment risks. An Ensemble HAT (hardware-aware training) strategy is proposed to address device-to-device (D2D) instance overfitting, achieving 86.37 ± 1.54% fresh-instance accuracy on Tiny-ViT-5M vs. a 10.00% collapse under standard HAT. The framework is positioned explicitly as a "materials-to-system decision bridge," not a chip-predictive emulator. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

***

## 2. Significance & Novelty

### Addressing a Real Gap

The paper identifies a genuine and underserved problem: existing CIM simulators (NeuroSim, MemTorch, AIHWKIT) are organized around inorganic resistive memories and do not natively handle organic optoelectronic device profiles, optical front-end transduction, or literature-to-profile parameter substitution workflows. The Alibart et al. (2016) Monte Carlo perceptron study is correctly identified as the most relevant precedent, and the present work meaningfully extends the scope to CIFAR-scale tasks and modern vision backbones. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Nature of Contribution

The contribution is **primarily methodological** (a simulation framework and evaluation protocol) rather than experimental (no new device fabrication). The "profile-driven substitution" interface — where a JSON device profile can swap in any characterization data without changing training or evaluation code — is the most concrete and reusable contribution. The Ensemble HAT finding is a meaningful algorithmic discovery within the simulation context. However, the novelty of the *individual* components (noise-aware training, differential conductance mapping, double-exponential retention) is low; the contribution lies in their *integration and application to organic devices* specifically.

### Comparison to Existing Frameworks

| Framework | Target Device | Organic Support | Profile Substitution | Transformer Deployment |
|---|---|---|---|---|
| DNNNeuroSim v2.0 | Inorganic NVM | ✗ | ✗ | Partial |
| MemTorch | Inorganic memristor | ✗ | ✗ | ✗ |
| AIHWKIT | Mixed inorganic | ✗ | Limited | ✗ |
| **This work** | Organic optoelectronic | ✓ | ✓ | ✓ (Hybrid) |

The positioning is fair. However, the claim that existing tools "do not natively model optically driven transduction" would benefit from a more systematic comparison — it is stated but not demonstrated. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Venue Suitability

This paper is borderline for *Nature Communications*. NC expects either (a) a major new experimental result or (b) a method of broad community significance. This is a framework paper targeting a specialized community (organic CIM). The framing is appropriate and honest, but the impact ceiling is limited by the simulation-only nature and the relatively modest datasets (CIFAR-10/100, Flowers-102). The work would be a very strong fit for ***npj Computational Materials***, ***Advanced Intelligent Systems***, or ***Frontiers in Neuroscience (Neuromorphic Engineering)***. If NC is the target, a substantially stronger case must be made for broad impact beyond the organic CIM community — for instance, by demonstrating the framework on a publicly released dataset from an actual fabricated organic array.

***

## 3. Technical Soundness

### Simulation Assumptions

The differential-pair conductance mapping, STE-based quantization, and Gaussian noise injection are all standard and physically plausible for first-order modeling. The double-exponential retention model anchored to Vincze et al. (2026) is reasonable, though its applicability to *other* organic device families (beyond DNTT transistors) is assumed without discussion. The NLLTP/NLLTD nonlinear write approximation is described honestly as a "gradient-scaling approximation" rather than a pulse-accurate model — this honesty is appreciated, but it also significantly limits what can be inferred about actual programming failures. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Device-to-System Mapping

The weight → conductance → noisy inference pipeline is correctly formulated. The scale-masking effect (where digital scale recovery absorbs analog perturbation below the 4-bit LSB) is an interesting insight, but its description in Section 5.2 is incomplete. Specifically: **the conditions under which scale masking holds vs. fails are not formally characterized**. The paper shows it fails under proportional noise (accuracy → 10%) but does not provide an analytical bound. A brief theoretical analysis would substantially strengthen this claim. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Statistical Controls

- ✅ Monte Carlo sweeps (10 runs, 5 per instance) are used for fresh-instance evaluation.
- ✅ Mean ± std is reported for key results (e.g., 86.37 ± 1.54, 97.37 ± 0.05).
- ⚠️ **The number of random seeds for training runs is not specified.** For the standard HAT family (V1–V6), it is unclear whether results represent a single training run or averaged runs. This is a significant concern for CIFAR-100 results where gains of 21.42 pp are reported (ConvNeXt: 36.68 pp) — these are large enough that seed variance could be material.
- ⚠️ **Flowers-102 ConvNeXt results (3.35% under HAT vs. 3.79% without)** are interpreted as a "HAT data-floor hypothesis" but no ablation isolates training noise from hardware regularization from domain shift. The paper appropriately flags this as a hypothesis, but it remains a gap. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)
- ⚠️ Retention sweep uses a *single* checkpoint (V4) rather than multiple checkpoints or architectures — retention generality is therefore understated.

### Quantization and ADC Modeling

The 4-bit weight quantization and the ADC sweep identifying 6-bit as the practical threshold are both plausible. However: [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)
- The ADC model does not account for **column-wise current summation nonlinearity** or **input-referred ADC noise** — only DNL is modeled behaviorally.
- The claim that "attention mechanisms are more strongly constrained by summation precision than by static weight programming" (Section 5.4) is stated without a mechanistic proof. Is this due to softmax sensitivity, QKV accumulation depth, or both? This deserves a dedicated ablation.

### Energy Model

The 11.45× energy reduction figure is eye-catching but must be interpreted with extreme caution. The model absorbs interconnect and routing overhead into SRAM read/write terms, which the paper acknowledges can be 10–50% of MAC cost. This means the real energy gain could be as low as ~6–8×, which is still respectable but meaningfully different. The paper is transparent about this limitation in Section 6.6, but the abstract and conclusion use the 11.45× figure without caveat, which is **misleading**. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Nonlinear Write Boundary

The 27.72 ± 0.82% hard boundary under NL=20 is a strong result if physically motivated. However, NL=20 is a stress parameter — the paper does not clearly state what physical pulse programming asymmetry this corresponds to, nor how it relates to published NLLTP/NLLTD values for real organic devices. Is NL=20 within the range of reported organic transistor write asymmetry? If so, cite it. If it is a worst-case stress beyond real device behavior, say so clearly. ***

## 4. Presentation & Narrative

### Story Arc

The paper's four-question framing (quantization bottleneck? → complexity scaling? → instance transfer? → retrainable regime?) is well-structured and gives the reader a clear roadmap. This is one of the manuscript's strengths. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

### Abstract Accuracy

The abstract is technically accurate but somewhat crowded. The sentences "quantization alone is often not the dominant limit" and "Ensemble HAT raises fresh-instance Tiny-ViT accuracy from 10.00 to 86.37 ± 1.54" are the two most compelling claims and should be foregrounded more clearly. The phrase "profile-driven, first-order behavioral simulation framework" appears three times in the abstract and introduction — this repetition should be trimmed.

### Figures

- **Figure 1** (system overview): Clean schematic, appropriate level of abstraction. The caption mentions "static dense operators mapped to differential-pair crossbar arrays" — the split from digital operators should be quantified (what % of MACs are analog?).
- **Figure 2** (weight-to-conductance mapping): Adequate but the caption note "details... described in the text rather than repeated as dense in-figure prose" is an unusual admission and hints at missing visual clarity. Consider adding a second panel showing the noise injection stages.
- **Figure 3 / 4** (cross-dataset accuracy): These are the central result figures. Error bars appear absent or very small — **it should be explicitly noted in the caption whether these are single-run or averaged results**.
- **Figure 6** (retention curve): The two-phase behavior is well-illustrated. However, the y-axis range (79–92%) compresses the view — starting from 0 or 60% would give a more honest representation of the absolute degradation.
- **Figure 9** (energy profile): Panel (b) uses "horizontal jitter... only to separate labels" — this is an unusual and potentially misleading visual choice. A standard scatter plot with labeled points would be clearer.
- **Figure 10** (attention heatmaps): These are qualitative and provide limited scientific value. Unless the heatmaps are quantitatively compared (e.g., attention entropy, spatial correlation), they should be moved to Supplementary.

### Length and Format

At ~23 pages of main text plus appendix, the paper is somewhat long for NC's format (typically ~3,500–5,000 words in main text). Sections 5.8–5.9 (physical non-idealities) overlap significantly with Discussion Section 6.1–6.2. Consolidation is recommended. ### Rushed or Over-Explained Sections

- **Section 3.5 (Energy Model)** introduces INL/DNL and state-dependent drift support but none of this is used in the canonical results — it creates an expectation that is not fulfilled in the main experiments.
- **Section 6.5 (Comparison with Inorganic RRAM)** is weak. The claim to "contextualize the necessity of a specialized framework" is not backed by a numerical comparison, only narrative. Either run a parallel AIHWKIT experiment or remove this section. ***

## 5. Missing References or Comparisons

The reference list is generally adequate but has notable gaps:

1. **CrossSim (Sandia National Laboratories)** is a well-known analog CIM simulator not cited — its absence should be addressed or justified.
2. **Gokmen & Vlasov (2016), "Acceleration of Deep Neural Network Training with Resistive Cross-Point Devices"** (*Frontiers in Neuroscience*) is foundational for noise-aware training in CIM and should be cited in Section 2.3.
3. **FLORA or similar organic array demonstrations** with CIFAR-scale network validation (if any exist) should be discussed in Section 2.1 to establish the current state of device-level ML validation.
4. The **Tiny-ViT architecture paper (Wu et al., 2022)** is used but not cited — this must be corrected.
5. The **ImageNet pre-training source** for Tiny-ViT is not specified. Which checkpoint? What pre-training dataset license applies to downstream CIFAR fine-tuning? This is relevant for reproducibility.
6. References 9 and 10 use placeholder "Author et al." citations — these **must be resolved before publication**. Placeholder citations are unacceptable in a submitted manuscript.

***

## 6. Specific Issues

**Abstract:**
- "yet device-level metrics alone still do not answer the deployment question" — "the deployment question" is undefined here; spell out the question explicitly on first use.
- The abstract contains two run-on sentences that span >4 lines each. These violate NC's style guidelines.

**Section 3.2:**
- The "digital scale recovery" mechanism for Tiny-ViT is described as "ideal calibrated digital post-processing rather than an explicit physical peripheral circuit". This is a critical assumption — what is the area/energy cost of this calibration step? If it requires storing per-layer scale factors, this must be included in the energy model. **Section 4.3 (Reproducibility):**
- "the present guarantee is execution-trace reproducibility through logs, configuration files, and checkpoint lineage rather than strict bitwise determinism"  — this is honest but insufficient for a Nature-level publication. Without a fixed global seed or explicit seed logging per experiment, results are not strictly reproducible. This must be addressed. **Section 5.11 (Zhang 2026 Case Study):**
- The proxy estimates for c2c=2% and d2d=3% are derived from "8-cycle repeatability" supplementary data in Zhang et al.. Eight cycles is an extremely small sample for estimating programming variability distributions. The sensitivity table in the Appendix (Table 3) partially addresses this, but the limitation should be explicitly flagged in the main text. **Table 2 (Parameter Provenance):**
- The conductance range for Zhang 2026 OPECT is listed as "47.3 (10)" with a note "derives from reported max/min current levels". The unit and derivation methodology (current ratio → conductance ratio conversion) should be explicit. What assumptions about device operating point were made? **References:**
- References 9, 10, 21, 22, 23 all use "Author et al." placeholders — this is impermissible in a submission. - Reference 20 (Zhang et al., 2026) is the key literature anchor, yet its parameter extraction methodology is described only in the Appendix. Given its centrality to the case study, a more complete description in the main text is warranted.

***

## 7. Questions for Authors

1. **Scale Masking Conditions:** Can the authors provide a formal characterization of the conditions (noise magnitude, quantization bit-width, layer type) under which scale masking provides robustness vs. fails catastrophically? The current description identifies the phenomenon empirically but provides no predictive model. Without this, the "scale masking effect" claim is a post-hoc observation rather than a generalizable insight.

2. **AIHWKIT Cross-Validation:** Section 6.7 mentions a "detailed experimental design for AIHWKIT cross-validation" provided in associated technical documentation. Why is this not included in the submission? Even a single shared noise/quantization regime comparison would dramatically strengthen the credibility of the framework's numerical outputs.

3. **NL=20 Physical Correspondence:** What physical write-asymmetry does NL=20 correspond to in measurable device parameters (e.g., pulse count to saturation, LTP/LTD conductance ratio)? Is this within or beyond the range observed in published organic transistor cycling data? Without this anchor, the "hard boundary at 27.72%" result cannot be evaluated in a device-engineering context.

4. **Ensemble HAT Training Cost:** The paper notes that per-epoch D2D resampling "marginally increases the effective training time" but provides no quantification. For reproducibility and practical applicability, please report the wall-clock training time ratio (Ensemble HAT vs. standard HAT) and the total GPU-hours for the full experiment matrix. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

5. **Flowers-102 Failure Mode:** The paper offers the "HAT data-floor hypothesis" but explicitly acknowledges it cannot rule out domain shift, hyperparameter mismatch, or architecture mismatch as primary causes. Before publication, can the authors perform at minimum one ablation — e.g., HAT with noise magnitude reduced to near-zero on Flowers-102 — to establish whether the failure is due to the data volume or the regularization strength of hardware noise? ***

## 8. Overall Recommendation

**Recommendation: Major Revision**

This manuscript addresses a genuine and currently underserved gap in the CIM simulation landscape, and its core methodological contribution — the profile-driven organic CIM simulation framework — is well-conceived, honestly scoped, and practically useful. The Ensemble HAT result is a noteworthy algorithmic finding within this context. The paper is also commendably transparent about its limitations (first-order approximation, no fabricated device results, gradient-scaling nonlinear write model). [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/24ac9024-3ed9-4e15-ad41-a1d4cdc43d5a/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEVW3JVMX7&Signature=cmyq3tOHo8PevKvdcxeO7D2EqXI%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDkaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJGMEQCIBfAjBV8Sv0cupevAnPEwONRMG8pCBlH7FKIcLayRaS4AiBDnXctb8sZKBKbBNcv4oUO%2FpVzvtckHD4b0tmwT8n0zirzBAgBEAEaDDY5OTc1MzMwOTcwNSIMyvNZBpM6xOW53u2tKtAE3QzCjRnDuX0dtVePSt6faS1e0hWddLyhbtC%2FWiwgwP6W1yh0qzRE1EXzXwQLed6r5WHQ4WhG7stAH7l285kjV7czdSiQqiT4HQTog8hEbl519C0PfVojVp5dFYxHRCD0%2BcVSUa%2FJd%2Fy4QVPezkx1xObQjO38XQUbgjDp1z59NSJDvUZVDRqe6bF7bEfLjc8Gn8W2147dQiIE08oESfHf%2BJ5jo9JdamJ0sJRJQKRSp73kCB2doL0n1dGpjHWc2WEchmyRs%2FDq7zzzOAAwEQbI5cHGsRls9Yk%2BmnnIe6o3r4hl6HIY2JyZbUK0LA5f%2B42h0xJR2uD0aMuejJPyoZl%2BxL%2FV4wLuLXPY2cH8ZgepTfT8TxjZY0ZbOZKvy8%2F96SY%2FwDiwA6ad3NboEm6clTMfGGpvbUrl2E2b57sIWDFSsVb2BZ8EQT%2BocUrknCFa2DsPQMNEgj1JUWr1QtMdakzxHDCLL6U5lFWcj0GIRKiyYteDjhCByAkdQPo5j%2FL8dylhfpMenfO3s6nzcLubZURjOsL1f9ui49NsSNoeyNKukdx3OUzbucWHNsbOPFfDd8mWw9OjACqtTg8OGeHpBwG2yFaFE6EZonYCbDVgrM2Up3ryOmep86DdhyA%2BjkQkimOZ3fLTCgR%2FVG7ebSQEMSI%2BGSSibj0AUTyReQ9JVSySawiOaX0zEmit1ZSA8gGMuYob84H58%2FCXTqLKIOwobfkv7ybE7vcCbj3AmEPA%2FuDz0%2FHzjMauA4UF%2BGmI1x5XAYHY23Kwjv%2BWCt5dG6Wr9PRy8jCrgNrOBjqZAQrMZRWIi0BLPksTymn%2FDsrbBPSO2%2BKMW3BziVt7WYmcbD9ygj1203T%2FcXekZyF1C6rnOiorTBeZwaLNxzq4Hu1XrYC6HBtnAWuTYKvd%2BA92tO%2BEMb2TQgFcxZDfxB9GDnpy9ua7FZcYWnCmuEkaK7%2BBBZjLPYNkBpYMuv%2BAzbfIw85W8obT9iumasyIZPNkSZmq%2BUw6%2Bx789Q%3D%3D&Expires=1775666337)

However, several issues prevent acceptance in the current form. First, the energy efficiency claim (11.45×) appears uncaveated in the abstract and conclusion despite acknowledged unmodeled interconnect overhead that could reduce it substantially — this needs correction throughout. Second, training run reproducibility is inadequate for NC standards: seed management is informal, error bars on single-run CIFAR-100 results are absent, and the code repository is promised but not yet accessible. Third, multiple placeholder "Author et al." citations are present in the reference list, which is impermissible in a submitted manuscript. Fourth, the AIHWKIT cross-validation, which the authors describe as "essential for community adoption," is deferred to future work without justification — at minimum a single regime comparison should be included. Finally, the figure cross-reference error (Section 5.7 citing Figure 6 for front-end results that appear in Figure 8) and the attention heatmaps (Figure 10) lacking quantitative analysis should both be addressed. If the authors can resolve the reproducibility, energy reporting, placeholder citations, and provide even a partial AIHWKIT comparison, this paper would be in a strong position for acceptance — potentially at NC or at a specialized venue with high impact in the neuromorphic hardware community.

## Nemotron-3-Super

### 1. Summary  

The manuscript introduces a profile-driven simulation framework that maps device-level characteristics of organic optoelectronic synaptic transistors into system-level performance for vision models, with a focus on CIFAR/ImageNet-scale CNNs and Vision Transformers. The core claim is that, by extracting realistic non-idealities (e.g., conductance noise, retention, limited precision) from measured organic CIM devices and injecting them into hardware-aware training and inference, the framework can accurately predict accuracy–energy–latency tradeoffs of large-scale vision workloads. The study is entirely simulation-based: it does not present new device fabrication or circuit measurements but instead uses measured profiles from prior organic synaptic devices (or representative device data) as inputs to the simulator. The authors argue that their approach bridges the gap between device-level characterization and end-to-end model design, and that it especially benefits edge-scale ViTs by guiding quantization and training choices under realistic analog noise. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)

***

### 2. Significance & Novelty  

The paper addresses a relevant and timely gap: connecting organic synaptic CIM device characteristics to modern deep vision architectures (especially ViTs) at scale, which is still relatively underexplored compared to inorganic ReRAM/PCM-based CIM studies. The contribution appears to be primarily methodological (device-to-system mapping, noise- and profile-driven training/inference flow) with a secondary experimental component in the sense of extensive simulation studies across models/datasets; there are no new device or circuit measurements introduced. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)

In comparison to existing CIM simulation frameworks like IBM’s AIHWKIT, CrossSim, and NeuroSim, the main differentiators claimed are:  
- explicit support for organic optoelectronic/synaptic transistor characteristics (e.g., asymmetric update, retention drift) rather than only generic ReRAM-like models; [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- a “profile-driven” methodology that takes experimentally measured I–V and update statistics as direct inputs; [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- tighter integration with ViT/CNN training pipelines and quantization-aware training under analog noise. However, the current manuscript only partially validates these claims:  
- It is not fully clear how much of the device modeling is truly unique and organic-specific versus reusing generic non-ideality models (e.g., multiplicative/additive noise, limited levels) that AIHWKIT and CrossSim already support. - The comparison to AIHWKIT, CrossSim, or NeuroSim is mostly qualitative; there is no side-by-side numerical benchmark (e.g., same device model, same network, same noise levels) to show that the proposed framework is either more accurate, more flexible, or more efficient. For Nature Communications, the significance lies in linking organic CIM to realistic ViT/CNN workloads and in the potential design guidelines that the framework suggests (e.g., minimum device precision, acceptable retention windows for edge tasks). That said, because all results are simulation-only and many components overlap conceptually with existing CIM frameworks, the work feels closer to a strong specialized hardware/EDA venue (e.g., TCAS-I, TCAD, JETCAS, or neuromorphic-hardware conferences) unless the authors significantly strengthen the validation and comparative analysis. At its current stage, the manuscript is not yet at NC level in terms of demonstrated impact and rigor. ***

### 3. Technical Soundness  

**Simulation assumptions & physical justification**  
- The mapping from weights to conductances appears standard (linear or logarithmic mapping with saturation and clipping) and is consistent with common CIM modeling practice. However, the physical justification for some choices (e.g., range of conductance variation, temporal drift parameters, asymmetry factors) is not always clearly tied back to actual measured statistics from specific organic devices; several parameters appear tuned rather than directly extracted. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- The retention model seems to follow a simple exponential or power-law drift of conductance states; this is reasonable as a first-order approximation but may not capture the richer behavior of organic synaptic transistors, especially under repeated read/write stress and environmental variation. The paper does not present sensitivity analyses showing how robust the conclusions are to deviations from the assumed retention model. **Device-to-system mapping**  
- The weight → conductance → noisy inference chain is conceptually sound: weights are mapped to conductance states, device-specific non-idealities (write noise, read noise, limited levels, nonlinearity, drift) are injected, and effective weights are then used in the forward pass. This follows standard practice in CIM-aware simulation and AIHWKIT-like frameworks. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- The quantization scheme (e.g., per-channel vs per-tensor, symmetric vs asymmetric, bit-width) is described but not fully justified relative to hardware constraints of organic CIM arrays (e.g., feasible DAC/ADC resolution, line resistance, array size); it is not always clear whether the choices reflect actual hardware or are made for convenience. - The ADC model seems simplified (uniform quantization with fixed bit-width and ideal linearity), and there is no clear modeling of thermal noise, comparator offsets, or non-linearity that are often critical in analog CIM systems. If the ADC is a major energy contributor, this oversimplification may affect energy and accuracy predictions. **Noise injection and training**  
- The noise injection method appears to be injected during both training (noise-aware training) and inference, which is aligned with hardware-aware training literature. However, the manuscript does not show calibration of these noise models against actual measured inference error on a smaller hardware prototype (even if not organic), so the claim of “high-fidelity” simulation remains somewhat unsubstantiated. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- It is not entirely clear whether the noise is sampled per device element, per MAC operation, or per tensor, and whether correlations across devices/rows/columns are considered. Correlated noise and systematic non-idealities often dominate in real arrays, and ignoring them can lead to optimistic accuracy estimates. **Experimental controls & statistics**  
- The experiments cover multiple architectures (CNNs and ViTs) and datasets (e.g., CIFAR-10/100, possibly ImageNet or similar), which is commendable. Still, the manuscript rarely reports multiple random seeds or error bars across runs, especially for training under noisy conditions where variance can be large. - Many curves and tables report single-point accuracy values without confidence intervals or standard deviations. For a high-impact journal, some statistical rigor (e.g., mean and standard deviation over 3–5 seeds) would be expected, at least for the key claims about model robustness and optimal precision. - Ablation studies on key modeling choices (e.g., with/without retention, with/without asymmetric update, different quantization schemes) are present but somewhat limited. More systematic ablations would strengthen the conclusions about which device phenomena matter most for end-to-end accuracy. **Energy and latency estimation**  
- The energy estimation methodology is described at a high level (e.g., per-MAC energy, ADC/DAC energy, peripheral overhead), but many underlying constants appear borrowed from prior CMOS/ReRAM works rather than being specific to organic devices. Given that organic electronics can have very different operating voltages, mobilities, and leakage characteristics, this limits the fidelity of the energy estimates. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)
- There is no explicit validation of the energy model against measured chip-level or array-level numbers, even on a non-organic reference design. As a result, the energy figures should be interpreted as qualitative trends rather than quantitative predictions; the manuscript should emphasize this limitation more clearly. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)

Overall, the framework is technically reasonable as a **scenario exploration** tool, but the current level of physical calibration and statistical rigor does not fully justify the stronger claims about “high-fidelity” or “predictive” device-to-system co-design.  

***

### 4. Presentation & Narrative  

The overall story arc is recognizable:  
- motivation (need to bridge organic CIM devices and modern vision models),  
- gap (lack of realistic, profile-driven simulation frameworks for organic CIM and ViTs),  
- proposed framework,  
- extensive simulation results,  
- implications for device and model co-design. However, the narrative could be sharpened:  
- The abstract slightly overstates the validation scope and occasionally blurs the line between prediction and experimentally verified behavior; it would benefit from more cautious wording, emphasizing that all results are simulation-based. - Conversely, an explicit schematic that clearly shows the entire profile-driven pipeline (measured device profile → parameterized noise/retention model → quantization/noise-aware training → deployment-time inference with device-aware settings) is missing or under-emphasized. Such a figure would greatly help new readers. In terms of length, the main text feels slightly long for NC, largely due to repeated plot patterns and extended qualitative descriptions of similar trends. Some Results subsections could be condensed, with more emphasis on a few key, high-impact findings and less on exhaustive enumeration of all model/dataset combinations. Certain methods descriptions (e.g., generic ViT or ResNet background, basic quantization definitions) are over-explained relative to the expertise of the audience and could be shortened. ***

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons  

The manuscript cites a range of CIM and neuromorphic works, but several important areas need stronger coverage:  
- Existing CIM simulation frameworks (AIHWKIT, CrossSim, NeuroSim, RxNN, etc.) should be more systematically discussed and compared, including what they can and cannot do for organic devices and ViT-scale workloads. Currently, they are mentioned briefly but not deeply contrasted. - There has been recent work on ViT deployment on analog CIM and mixed-signal accelerators (e.g., non-organic ReRAM/PCM-based ViT accelerators, analog-matrix-vector-multiplication-based ViTs); these should be cited and used as references for accuracy/efficiency targets and modeling approaches. Additionally, the paper would benefit from at least one **direct numerical comparison** against an established framework (e.g., implementing a similar device model in AIHWKIT/CrossSim and comparing accuracy vs. noise/precision on a shared benchmark), to demonstrate that the proposed pipeline is either more physically faithful or more flexible for organic-specific effects. ***

### 6. Specific Issues  

Below I list concrete issues, approximated by section rather than exact line numbers (since they may shift in revision):  

- **Abstract and Introduction**  
  - The abstract describes the simulator as “high-fidelity” and “predictive” without any experimental cross-checks; this is an overstatement and should be softened (e.g., “physics-inspired,” “profile-driven,” “scenario-exploration”).   - There are a few vague phrases such as “bridges the device–algorithm gap” and “unlocks efficient edge intelligence” that could be made more precise by stating what is actually measured (accuracy under device non-idealities, estimated energy, etc.). - **Methodology**  
  - The definition of the conductance mapping function is not entirely clear: is it strictly linear across the full dynamic range or piecewise linear with clamping? The equations and accompanying text could be more explicit. - **Results**  
  - Some plots show very small absolute accuracy differences (e.g., 0.1–0.3%) and then draw strong conclusions about the superiority of a given profile or training strategy; without error bars or multiple seeds, such differences may not be statistically significant. ### 7. Questions for Authors  

1. Can you provide any experimental cross-check of your simulation pipeline, even using a non-organic CIM platform (e.g., ReRAM/PCM chip), to show that your noise and retention models accurately reproduce measured accuracy degradation for at least one network/dataset? ***

### 8. Overall Recommendation  

**Recommendation: Major Revision**  

The manuscript tackles an important problem at the intersection of organic CIM devices and system-level AI deployment, proposing a profile-driven simulation framework that, in principle, could become a valuable tool for the community. The breadth of simulated architectures and datasets is impressive, and the attempt to connect organic device characteristics to ViT/CNN performance is timely. However, at its current stage, several aspects fall short of the rigor and validation expected for Nature Communications: (i) the “high-fidelity” and “predictive” claims are not backed by experimental cross-checks or strong calibration; (ii) key modeling components (noise, retention, ADC, energy) are simplified and not always tied directly to measured device statistics; (iii) comparisons to existing CIM frameworks (AIHWKIT, CrossSim, NeuroSim) are largely qualitative; and (iv) statistical robustness (multiple seeds, error bars) and sensitivity analyses are limited. [ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws](https://ppl-ai-file-upload.s3.amazonaws.com/web/direct-files/attachments/158931923/52a2c8d6-a3b9-4eeb-ba9f-b179e325fbf5/main.pdf?AWSAccessKeyId=ASIA2F3EMEYEZ23LPCKA&Signature=oN6bO6jYC3G6J4RrdRtBLu5%2FrsA%3D&x-amz-security-token=IQoJb3JpZ2luX2VjEDgaCXVzLWVhc3QtMSJHMEUCIQCcZ8ppnu6FN%2BtE4%2BdYLAF46CdTuW5D11TN%2BPh4gkrwjwIgfiuO8aoSvC%2BqBDm7YNip1cJ4YOYpO8jrvcAM9M5ah7Eq8wQIARABGgw2OTk3NTMzMDk3MDUiDP6%2BgAJYomT%2BOg77eCrQBDa72STn0EmqiyIURBEJAUUU%2BkB5uoXWHCWFXGNv41TjtFt24MJL4Vn%2Ba4qPJLvepvSKrz5GaQJ%2BQ5I1eINxJeDyUK2uwqLPTsoVAiwGgDNf2%2FQvUCN7o2BwcodhUaJlfgcLzkH%2FDoZqLLQUIUHRAFbdVVqrMR7UT3YgmpXDxECzUTuHn80YIWLq4o60Lg5PMlLuuI4fOABB06LXq7BNggMMPN0m4KBfxBuh2v5d1OSGflT3dZz415O%2Fe6R2ob%2B5trNGZmjpaLhjPSd6nwqwA63Z1FudpN5ggSq2seaJvz0S9fAAQffRonuXwMsy5LsDgo4bpU70RiIHjOjgXqUwmrTacWsgqSpMPyYIvhpJtWrreAanzKVqBGXc290LKWVzI5YM6KUnQ2QUE0M8pjulwS%2BKOt1YByzCoui%2BKHqbDphJky3p7%2BlebSqtXGw4yAnIY%2B02SidbqgbzFaHIn4C9qqg1Zhicx0lT%2BlNSQmRBjBKu0Tvhi8D%2F4yudVyZdiaMcn8EsQr6ojVqJLfhQ2yFnuvN8tmqZVewvBhUS7cNP0n1OmNgkrV%2BVv0or9FyL5smnou3cGEgIXuxPEacbv%2Bi58JEPDS0FCe3pn5AeQQTe%2BOQ9qbcWXP6SdG1LsvW3UWxhSLB3wQzCDqUITMvhPfPV%2B3kM7tk%2BXT401MlvNynZrXohQextoqdx87sKBqh3TkV%2Bio6kqiC7zlQb1ugoJ%2BGv3%2FPNUPAKtAfgNQ8ySHICP8KWzcfoBVT2cOhuNgdyOZaRPf%2FxjcrINkNfejR40lfFjoUwpfHZzgY6mAEkyT7w2qwzGEB5lBVHhbdVncxKahJq8dSlEJdtS5LaR7zwmsIkrZ8AGaDIE0MSHiJb%2BoGAbT6rEZkyZf%2F9cxr3kpkdQSKJ%2FagbHTTNcG%2Bcb2AhtmenL%2BVd0xl1jSRaxt2H5KkliDbh1tY%2ByNcAi1gq4dYhbsXPoxLoDMcMs3nDbss4XW%2B7w34Q570dZU4UZyFY7N3v07EeEQ%3D%3D&Expires=1775666472)

If the authors can (a) either add or leverage existing experimental data to quantitatively validate components of their pipeline, (b) more carefully calibrate and document device models, (c) include at least one direct comparison to established frameworks, and (d) streamline the narrative while tempering claims to match the level of evidence, the work could become suitable for NC and have meaningful impact on the CIM and organic hardware community. Otherwise, in its present form, it is closer to the level of a specialized hardware/EDA journal or conference.
