Would you like help drafting a marked-up PDF or detailed line-by-line comments you can send to the authors/advisor?

## DeepSeek-V3.2

尊敬的编辑和作者：

感谢您给我机会审阅这篇题为《Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision》的稿件。我是一名在模拟人工智能硬件、有机电子器件和硬件感知训练领域有深入研究的学者。以下是我对这篇投稿给《自然-通讯》的稿件的详细评审意见。我将遵循您要求的评审结构。

### 1. 总结
本文提出了一种面向有机光电计算内存（CIM）推理的、硬件感知的、一阶行为模拟框架。该框架的核心目标是充当器件与系统之间的“决策桥梁”，通过可替换的配置文件，将文献提取或测量得到的器件特性（如电导窗口、噪声、保持特性）映射到任务级的精度和能量趋势上。论文的核心论点是：在边缘视觉部署中，主要瓶颈通常不是标称量化，而是转换器精度、任务复杂性、新鲜硬件实例的差异以及更复杂的器件物理特性（如状态相关噪声、非线性写入）。作者通过一系列实验，包括在ResNet-18、ConvNeXt-Tiny和Tiny-ViT-5M模型上对CIFAR-10/100和Flowers-102数据集的评估，来支持这一观点，并特别强调了集成硬件感知训练在解决实例过拟合问题上的有效性。

### 2. 意义与创新性
**优点：**
*   **填补明确空白：** 论文准确地指出了一个重要且未被充分探索的领域：现有的成熟CIM模拟器（如DNN+NeuroSim, MemTorch, AIHWKIT）主要围绕无机忆阻器设计，缺乏对有机光电器件特定问题（如光学前端、基于部分表征的配置文件替换、混合CNN/Transformer部署决策）的针对性支持。这项工作成功地填补了这一方法论空白。
*   **贡献明确：** 贡献主要是方法论上的，但具有重要的实际意义。提出了一种“配置文件驱动”的仿真工作流程，使得从器件测量到系统级评估的路径更加结构化。这为器件和架构研究人员提供了一个共同的语言和工具，用于在流片前进行风险评估。
*   **与现有工具定位清晰：** 作者明智地将自己的工作定位为对现有无机CIM模拟器的**补充**而非替代，强调了其在有机器件特定参数化和混合映射策略方面的专门性。这种定位是恰当且具有说服力的。
*   **《自然-通讯》级影响力：** 这项工作是跨学科的，结合了材料科学、器件物理、计算机架构和机器学习。它为快速发展的有机神经形态器件领域提供了急需的系统级视角，有助于引导材料研究面向实际部署挑战。其方法和发现对广泛的读者（从器件工程师到算法研究人员）都具有价值，符合《自然-通讯》的广泛读者定位。

**不足/疑问：**
*   虽然方法论是新颖的，但部分核心思想（如硬件感知训练、混合模拟/数字映射、考虑非理想因素的模拟）在更广泛的CIM文献中并非全新。论文需要更清晰地阐明，相较于将类似技术应用于有机领域，其**根本性创新**究竟在哪里。
*   “配置文件”接口的概念很有价值，但论文对其“验证”的描述停留在案例研究（Zhang 2026 OPECT）和敏感性分析上。一个更强大的验证应该包括与**至少一个**现有成熟模拟器（如AIHWKIT）在可比较的噪声/量化机制下进行基准测试，以证明其行为一致性。

### 3. 技术严谨性
**优点：**
*   **仿真假设：** 总体合理。论文明确声明了其“一阶行为模拟”的定位，并未声称是“芯片精确仿真”。对量化、C2C/D2D噪声、ADC分辨率和保持特性的建模是标准做法，且在领域内被广泛接受。对光学前端（光电响应、暗电流）和非线性写入（通过梯度缩放近似）的纳入是相关工作的重要延伸。
*   **实验控制：** 实验设计全面，包含充分的基线（FP32数字模型）和消融研究（例如，比较有无HAT、不同ADC位宽、不同噪声模型）。对每个检查点进行蒙特卡洛评估以报告均值和标准差是严谨的做法。
*   **能量模型：** 虽然简化，但其假设是明确的（例如，将互连开销吸收到内存访问成本中），并且为架构级权衡提供了有价值的见解。

**主要问题与顾虑：**
1.  **“缩放掩蔽”效应：** 第5.2节中关于“数字缩放恢复将有效模拟扰动压缩到4位LSB以下”的论断是本文的一个关键观察。然而，这需要更严格的物理解释或分析验证。这是所有模拟CIM系统的普遍特性，还是本框架中特定量化/映射方案的结果？这需要进一步澄清。
2.  **非线性写入模型：** 使用`NL_LTP/NL_LTD`作为STE后向传递的梯度缩放近似，是一种将实测非对称性纳入训练的实用方法。但作者必须更明确地强调，这是一种**训练时正则化技术**，而非对实际脉冲写入动力学的精确模拟。结果部分（5.8, 5.9）显示该模型在严重非线性下会导致硬故障，这引发了疑问：是Transformer本质上无法容忍这种失真，还是当前的梯度缩放近似不足以捕捉潜在的器件行为，从而无法进行有效的训练？需要更深入的讨论。
3.  **能量模型简化：** 承认未建模IR压降、寄生效应和详细路由开销是很好的做法（第6.6节）。然而，声称“11.45倍的能效提升”可能具有误导性，因为数字基线（FP32）是非常低效的比较对象。与更现实的数字量化基线（例如，INT8）进行对比，将使能效主张更具说服力。
4.  **Flowers-102上的HAT失败：** 第5.3节中将ConvNeXt-Tiny在Flowers-102上HAT性能下降归因于“数据量下限假设”和“正则化过于激进”。虽然合理，但这仍然是一个假设。需要更多的消融实验来排除其他原因，例如领域偏移、不恰当的超参数或架构不匹配。目前，将其作为一个“产生假设的失败案例”来呈现是合适的，但结论部分应稍微软化相关措辞。

### 4. 表述与叙述
*   **故事线：** 非常清晰。论文遵循了标准的“问题-差距-方法-结果-影响”结构。四个部署问题的组织使论述重点突出。
*   **摘要与结果：** 摘要准确地反映了核心发现，没有过度炒作。
*   **图表：** 从描述来看，图表（如能量分析、任务复杂度缩放、保持特性）似乎是恰当的。需要查看实际图表以评估其出版质量。图9的描述（能效分析）是必要的。
*   **篇幅与平衡：** 稿件篇幅适中，符合《自然-通讯》格式。然而，**第4节（实验设置）** 有些冗长，包含了过多可能更适合补充信息的细节（例如，V1-V8的确切定义）。可以精简，将部分细节移至方法或补充材料。相反，**第6节（讨论）** 非常出色，是论文的亮点，对结果进行了深思熟虑的整合和解读。

### 5. 缺失的参考文献或对比
*   应考虑引用更多最近关于**有机CIM阵列**和**ViT硬件加速**的研究。例如：
    *   **有机CIM阵列：** 除了Zhang等人（2026）的案例研究，是否有其他近期展示阵列级集成的有机光电CIM工作？引用它们可以加强研究背景。
    *   **ViT on Hardware：** 应引用更多关于Transformer模型在内存计算或模拟加速器上映射的前沿工作（例如，关于PIM上ViT的“Allspark”[17]和“EPIM”[16]已被引用，但可能还需要提及其他如“ViTALiTy”或“SpAtten”等相关工作，以展示对该领域更全面的把握）。
*   **模拟训练框架：** 虽然引用了IBM的AIHWKIT[11]，但可以更直接地讨论本文的配置文件驱动方法与AIHWKIT的“AnalogModel”和“AnalogSGD”等抽象之间的异同。这能进一步明确技术定位。

### 6. 具体问题（逐行）
*   **术语不一致：** 在第1页摘要和第5页，“hardware-aware training (HAT)”有时似乎特指本文使用的训练方法，但HAT在更广泛的文献中是一个通用术语。建议在首次使用时明确定义本文的HAT具体指什么（例如，“我们采用硬件感知训练，即在训练前向传递中注入预期的硬件噪声”）。
*   **图表引用格式：** 正文中多次出现“Fig. 6”、“Fig. 9”等引用，但在提供的文本中并未包含这些图表。请确保所有图表引用正确，并且在最终稿件中提供高质量的图表。
*   **第5.5节，保持力：** 描述“在1秒时从91.63%快速下降到82.66%”与“10秒至10,000秒之间保持在79%左右的广阔平台期”似乎存在矛盾。1秒后的下降是“快速”的吗？请检查措辞的准确性。
*   **第5.7节，核心价值结论：** 语句“Inverse-gamma compensation provides a physical-level regularization effect in low-light/dark scenarios”有些令人费解。补偿如何起到“正则化”作用？需要重新表述以更清晰地解释其机制（例如，“通过线性化信号，有助于保持动态范围”）。
*   **第6.1节：** 段落开头“The combined ResNet, ConvNeXt, and Tiny-ViT analyses revise the intuitive failure hierarchy...” 后面的句子似乎不完整（“10”和“97”后面缺失内容）。这看起来是文本提取错误，需要在原稿中核对并修正。
*   **附录A，表2：** 在“Zhang 2026 OPECT Case Study”一列下，`G_max/G_min`值为47.3，但`n_states`为34。从电导范围到有效状态数的映射关系需要简要说明（例如，是否是等间距量化？）。

### 7. 给作者的问题
1.  **配置文件工作流程的普适性：** 论文提出了一个“自动化配置文件拟合流程”（附录A.3）。然而，从原始器件测量（脉冲编程曲线、循环间统计等）到模拟配置文件参数的转换，在多大程度上是自动化的，又在多大程度上需要手动调整或专家判断？能否提供一个更具体的示例，说明如何从一篇典型器件论文的图表中提取这些参数？
2.  **仿真保真度验证：** 您将框架定位为“行为模拟”而非“芯片精确仿真”。为了建立可信度，是否有可能在**共同的噪声和量化机制**下，将您的框架与一个成熟的、经过验证的模拟器（如IBM的AIHWKIT）进行“苹果对苹果”的比较？即使目标器件不同，这种比较也能验证您模拟计算路径的基本正确性。
3.  **HAT在数据稀缺时失效的解释：** 对于Flowers-102，您假设HAT的失败是由于“数据量下限”导致正则化过于激进。您是否尝试过调整HAT噪声的强度（σ值）或使用更温和的正则化方案？如果HAT确实对数据量如此敏感，这对于将有机CIM部署到边缘视觉（通常数据有限）意味着什么？
4.  **未建模效应的影响：** 第6.6节恰当地列出了许多限制（IR压降、温度效应、光学非均匀性）。在这些因素中，您认为哪一个**最有可能**改变您关于主导瓶颈（例如，ADC精度 vs. 器件噪声）的结论？能否进行一个简单的敏感性分析来支持您的判断？

### 8. 总体建议
**决定：重大修改**

**理由：**
本文提出了一项及时、构思良好且执行扎实的研究，旨在解决有机神经形态计算领域一个切实存在的差距。其核心思想——一个连接部分器件表征与系统级性能评估的、可配置文件的模拟框架——具有很高的价值，并且很可能影响该领域的发展方向。方法学新颖，实验设计全面，讨论部分见解深刻。

然而，要达到《自然-通讯》的高标准，还需要进行实质性修改。主要问题在于需要更清晰地界定仿真预测与实验证据之间的界限，并加强某些关键主张的论证。具体而言：
1.  **验证与基准测试：** 强烈建议增加与一个成熟模拟器（如AIHWKIT）的对比分析，即使是在一个简化的、器件无关的设定下，以验证仿真核心的正确性。
2.  **澄清与严谨性：** 必须澄清“缩放掩蔽”效应的物理基础，并更明确地强调非线性写入模型是一种训练时近似。能量收益的主张应相对于更现实的数字基线（如INT8）进行阐述。
3.  **论述平衡：** 需要软化关于Flowers-102结果的因果断言，更明确地将其呈现为一个需要进一步研究的观察结果。
4.  **表述与细节：** 需要解决第6节中提到的文本不完整问题，精简实验设置部分，并确保所有图表引用正确且图表质量达到出版标准。

这项工作的核心贡献是坚实且有影响力的。经过上述修订，它将有潜力在《自然-通讯》上发表，并为跨器件、架构和算法研究社区提供重要的工具和见解。

## 豆包

# Manuscript Review for Nature Communications
**Reviewer #2** | Manuscript Title: Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision

---

## 1. Summary
This manuscript presents a profile-driven, hardware-aware behavioral simulation framework tailored for organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) inference for edge vision tasks. The core contribution is a PyTorch-based workflow that bridges partial organic device characterization (from literature or measurements) to system-level accuracy, energy, and deployment risk assessment for modern convolutional and transformer vision backbones, without modifying core training/evaluation code paths. The authors systematically evaluate the framework across ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M on CIFAR-10/100 and Flowers-102, identifying that converter precision, device-to-device (D2D) variability, state-dependent noise, and nonlinear write dynamics dominate deployment bottlenecks (rather than nominal quantization), and demonstrate that Ensemble Hardware-Aware Training (HAT) drastically improves fresh hardware instance transferability from 10.00% to 86.37±1.54%. The work positions the framework as a materials-to-system decision tool for organic optoelectronic CIM deployment, rather than a chip-predictive emulator.

---

## 2. Significance & Novelty
### Strengths
- **Meaningful Field Gap**: This work addresses a critical, understudied gap in the neuromorphic hardware community. Existing mature CIM simulators (NeuroSim, AIHWKIT, MemTorch) are optimized for inorganic resistive memories, and do not natively support organic optoelectronic device-specific needs: profile substitution from partial characterization, optical frontend modeling, and hybrid analog/digital mapping for modern CNN/transformer backbones. Meanwhile, organic device literature overwhelmingly focuses on device-level metrics, with system-level validation limited to small perceptrons or idealized mappings, leaving a disconnect between materials characterization and real-world edge deployment decisions. This work directly closes that gap.
- **Dual Methodological and Experimental Contribution**: The primary contribution is methodological: a flexible, profile-driven simulation framework purpose-built for organic optoelectronic CIM, with unified modeling of quantization, C2C/D2D variability, retention drift, ADC non-idealities, optical frontend effects, and nonlinear write dynamics. This is complemented by a rigorous, large-scale experimental evaluation across 3 modern vision architectures and 3 datasets of varying complexity, which provides actionable, deployment-relevant insights for both materials scientists and system designers.
- **Broad Impact for NC Readership**: Nature Communications targets a cross-disciplinary audience spanning materials science, device engineering, circuit design, and AI systems. This work is uniquely positioned to serve all these communities: it provides materials researchers with a tool to prioritize device optimization targets, and system designers with a transparent framework to assess organic CIM viability for state-of-the-art edge vision models. The findings on transformer fragility to hardware non-idealities and Ensemble HAT for cross-instance generalization are also broadly relevant to the analog AI hardware community.

### Limitations & Concerns
- **Novelty Boundaries**: The core simulation logic (layer replacement, forward-path perturbation, hardware-aware training) builds on established inorganic CIM simulator paradigms, with specialization for organic devices. While this specialization is meaningful, the paper does not clearly benchmark its framework against state-of-the-art simulators (e.g., CrossSim, which is unmentioned) on shared inorganic device benchmarks to quantify functional parity and organic-specific improvements.
- **Venue Suitability**: This is a simulation-only study with no new device fabrication or hardware measurement results. While the methodological and system-level insights are strong, NC typically prioritizes works with combined methodological advances and experimental validation. The current manuscript would be significantly strengthened by validation against measured array data, or at minimum a head-to-head benchmark against a mature CIM simulator on a shared task. That said, the cross-disciplinary impact and actionable insights for multiple communities still make it a strong candidate for NC, conditional on major revisions.

---

## 3. Technical Soundness
### Strengths
- **Physically Grounded Modeling**: Most core simulation assumptions are anchored to published organic device literature, with full parameter provenance documented in the Appendix. The differential conductance mapping, straight-through estimator (STE) for quantization, double-exponential retention model, and behavioral ADC modeling align with standard analog CIM simulation practices, adapted appropriately for organic device operating regimes. The side-by-side comparison of uniform vs. state-dependent retention models (with <0.1pp accuracy difference) also adds rigor to the retention modeling choices.
- **Rigorous Experimental Design**: The authors establish clear FP32 digital baselines for all model-dataset combinations, use Monte Carlo resampling for stochastic inference evaluations, and include systematic ablation studies across quantization, noise, converter precision, retention, and training strategies. The separation of canonical experiments from stress tests ensures core conclusions are not conflated with edge-case results.
- **Statistical Rigor**: Key results include standard deviations from repeated Monte Carlo runs (e.g., Ensemble HAT, proportional noise HAT), and the 2D sensitivity sweep for the Zhang 2026 profile proxy estimates adds confidence in the zero-shot transfer results.

### Critical Concerns
- **Overly Idealized Core Simulation Assumptions**: The canonical experiments rely on uniform, state-independent noise, but the authors show that models trained under this assumption collapse to 10% accuracy when evaluated under state-dependent proportional noise—an effect widely observed in real organic synaptic devices. This calls into question the generalizability of the paper’s core conclusions (e.g., "quantization alone is not the dominant limit") which are derived from the uniform noise regime. The paper also explicitly omits modeling of IR drop, sneak-path currents, temperature effects, and optical non-uniformity, all of which are critical non-idealities in real organic CIM arrays, and may lead to overly optimistic accuracy and energy predictions. While these limitations are acknowledged in the Discussion, they are not addressed in the core experimental validation, and their impact on the paper’s conclusions is not quantified.
- **Incomplete Nonlinear Write Modeling**: The nonlinear write implementation uses a first-order gradient-scaling approximation, rather than pulse-accurate modeling of organic device programming dynamics. The authors find that severe nonlinearity (NL=2.0) is a "hard boundary" for accuracy, but do not disentangle whether this is an artifact of the simplified gradient-scaling model, or a fundamental physical limit of organic devices. This is a critical ambiguity for the paper’s core deployment-focused claims.
- **Reproducibility Limitations**: The authors acknowledge that the codebase lacks a project-wide random seed interface, with only "execution-trace reproducibility" via logs and checkpoints. For a simulation-focused paper intended as a community tool, strict bitwise reproducibility via fixed random seeds is a non-negotiable requirement for independent validation of results.
- **Inadequate Energy Model Validation**: The energy model absorbs interconnect overhead into SRAM access terms, does not separately account for routing costs between analog and digital blocks, and provides no head-to-head comparison of the 11.45x energy reduction against published digital or inorganic CIM accelerator benchmarks for Tiny-ViT. The energy breakdown also reports that ADC/DAC/buffer costs account for 0.0% of total energy, which is physically unrealistic for analog CIM systems and suggests a critical error in the energy profiler implementation.
- **Missing Ablations**: The paper does not include ablation studies for key design choices, such as the hybrid analog/digital operator split for Tiny-ViT, the impact of differential pair mapping on accuracy/energy, or the contribution of digital scale recovery to the "scale masking" effect. These ablations are necessary to validate the authors’ interpretation of their results.

---

## 4. Presentation & Narrative
### Strengths
- **Clear Story Arc**: The manuscript follows a logical, linear narrative: Problem (device metrics do not answer deployment questions) → Gap (existing simulators do not support organic optoelectronic CIM needs) → Solution (profile-driven simulation framework) → Experimental Validation → Key Findings → Limitations & Future Work. The problem statement is clearly articulated in the Introduction, and the Discussion does an excellent job of contextualizing the results, acknowledging limitations, and avoiding overclaiming.
- **Accurate Abstract**: The abstract faithfully reflects the paper’s core methodology, key positive and negative results, and overall contribution, without overstating the work’s scope (e.g., explicitly noting it is not a chip-predictive emulator).
- **Transparent Limitations**: The Discussion includes a thorough, honest section on the framework’s limitations, which is rare and commendable for a manuscript submission.

### Critical Concerns
- **Figure Quality & Clarity**: Multiple figures have critical formatting, labeling, and readability issues that make them unsuitable for publication:
  - Figures 3, 4, 6, and 8 lack clear axis labels, units, and legends (e.g., Figure 6 has no y-axis label for accuracy; Figure 3’s y-axis is unlabeled; Figure 8’s corruption types are undefined).
  - Figure 7 has misaligned x/y axis labels and inconsistent formatting between the two panels.
  - Figure 9 contains numerical inconsistencies (e.g., "Total cost 3137" with no units, conflicting with the 274 μJ total inference cost cited in the text; 0.0% energy share for ADC/DAC, which is physically unrealistic) and poor axis scaling.
  - Figure 10’s attention heatmaps lack context: no input image reference, no color scale definition, no dataset/sample specification, making the qualitative claim uninterpretable.
- **Manuscript Length**: At 19 pages of main text (excluding references and appendix), the manuscript is significantly longer than Nature Communications’ typical main text limit of 8 pages. Large sections (e.g., detailed experiment matrix design, parameter provenance, automated profile fitting pipeline) can be moved to the Supplementary Information, with only key insights retained in the main text.
- **Uneven Pacing**: The Results section is overly fragmented into 11 subsections, many of which can be merged (e.g., 5.8 Physical Non-Idealities and 5.9 HAT Recovery under Physical Stress; 5.2 Quantization and 5.4 ADC Thresholds). The Related Work section provides excellent context, but the Methodology section’s hybrid mapping description is overly verbose, while critical details of the noise injection and retention modeling are buried in the text rather than highlighted.
- **Formatting Errors**: The manuscript is riddled with numerical formatting errors: missing ± symbols for error bars (e.g., 86.371.54% in the Abstract), incorrect decimal separators (273:94 μJ), misaligned table columns (Table 1), and inconsistent notation for parameters (e.g., σC2C vs σc2c across the text and tables).

---

## 5. Missing References or Comparisons
1. **Missing Mainstream CIM Simulator Comparison**: The manuscript fails to cite or compare against CrossSim, one of the most widely used open-source CIM simulators for analog AI hardware. A head-to-head comparison (functional parity, organic-specific feature support) is required to contextualize the framework’s novelty relative to the state of the art.
2. **Incomplete Organic CIM System-Level Literature**: The manuscript only cites Alibart et al. 2016 for prior organic variability-aware simulation, and omits recent (2023–2025) works on system-level modeling and validation of organic synaptic devices for neuromorphic computing. These works must be cited and contextualized relative to the proposed framework.
3. **Missing ViT-on-CIM Prior Work**: The manuscript’s discussion of transformer mapping to CIM only cites 3 references, and omits key recent works on hardware-aware training and analog deployment of vision transformers for ReRAM CIM, including studies on multi-instance training and D2D variability mitigation for transformers. These works are critical for contextualizing the Ensemble HAT contribution.
4. **Nonlinear Write Modeling Literature**: The manuscript’s gradient-scaling approach to nonlinear write modeling does not cite or compare against established behavioral models for organic synaptic device programming dynamics, which are required to justify the modeling choice and its limitations.
5. **Optical Frontend Modeling**: The discussion of inverse-gamma compensation for the organic phototransistor frontend lacks citations to prior work on linearization and noise mitigation for optoelectronic synaptic arrays, which is necessary to contextualize the tradeoff analysis.

---

## 6. Specific Issues
1. **Abstract**: Multiple numerical formatting errors: missing ± symbols for all error bars (e.g., "86.371.54%" → "86.37±1.54%", "97.370.05%" → "97.37±0.05%", "27.72 0.82%" → "27.72±0.82%").
2. **Table 1**: Severe column misalignment: the row "Tiny-ViT-5M ConvNeXt-Tiny CIFAR-10 CIFAR-100 97.48 64.12" merges columns incorrectly, making the baseline results uninterpretable.
3. **Section 3.3**: The retention model is anchored to Vincze et al. [18], a 2026 paper with the same submission date as this manuscript. This reference is inaccessible to readers, so the full double-exponential decay parameters and device details must be added to the Appendix, or replaced with a peer-reviewed, published reference.
4. **Section 5.4**: The claim "At 4-bit ADC resolution, accuracy drops to 27%. Raising the converter to 6-bit restores accuracy to above 80%" lacks critical context: no specification of the model, dataset, or experimental configuration, and no reported standard deviation.
5. **Section 5.5**: Figure 6 includes a ConvNeXt C9 retention curve, but the text only discusses the Tiny-ViT V4 result, with no explanation of the ConvNeXt data. The figure also lacks a y-axis label for accuracy (%).
6. **Section 5.10**: The energy model claims ADC/DAC/buffer costs account for 0.0% of total energy, which is physically impossible for analog CIM systems. This indicates a critical implementation error in the energy profiler that must be fixed and revalidated. The text also has a typo: "273:94 J" → "273.94 μJ".
7. **Appendix Table 3**: All rows show identical accuracy values across C2C variations. While the text provides an explanation, the table must include statistical test results (e.g., p-values) to confirm no significant difference between conditions, rather than reporting identical numerical values which appear to be a formatting error.
8. **Section 5.6**: The phrase "collapses to near-random performance" is used before defining the numerical value (10.00%), leading to ambiguity. The numerical value must be cited on first mention.
9. **Section 2.3**: The operator mapping justification cites only ReRAM-focused references [15–17], with no citations to organic CIM operator mapping studies. Relevant organic-specific literature must be added.
10. **Section 7 Conclusion**: The Zhang 2026 OPECT case study result (88.53% accuracy) does not specify the target dataset, which is required for interpretability.

---

## 7. Questions for Authors
1. The core conclusions of the paper are derived from canonical experiments using uniform, state-independent noise, but the authors show that models trained under this regime collapse to 10% accuracy when evaluated under state-dependent proportional noise—an effect ubiquitous in real organic synaptic devices. How do you assess the generalizability of your core findings (e.g., quantization not being the dominant bottleneck) to physically realistic device noise regimes? Do you plan to make proportional state-dependent noise the default setting for your canonical experiments in future work?
2. Your Ensemble HAT method delivers dramatic improvements in fresh hardware instance transferability, but you note that it incurs training overhead due to per-epoch D2D mask resampling. Can you quantify the exact increase in training time and compute cost relative to standard HAT? Have you explored more lightweight strategies to achieve cross-instance generalization without per-epoch resampling?
3. Your framework omits modeling of critical array-level non-idealities including IR drop, sneak-path currents, and temperature-dependent device shifts, all of which are significant in real organic CIM arrays. How do you expect these unmodeled effects to impact your core accuracy and energy efficiency conclusions? Do you have plans to integrate these physical effects into the framework?
4. You validate the profile-driven framework using a literature-derived device profile from Zhang 2026, but note that the C2C/D2D noise parameters are proxy estimates, not measured full-array noise distributions. Do you have plans to validate the framework’s prediction accuracy using fully characterized, measured data from a fabricated organic optoelectronic synaptic array? Is there a plan to benchmark the simulator’s predictions against post-fabrication measurement results?
5. You find that severe nonlinear write (NL=2.0) remains a hard accuracy boundary even after HAT retraining. Do you attribute this limitation to your first-order gradient-scaling approximation of nonlinear write dynamics, or to a fundamental physical limit of organic synaptic devices? Have you explored more advanced modeling or training strategies to mitigate this bottleneck?

---

## 8. Overall Recommendation
**Recommendation: Major Revision**

This manuscript addresses a critical, unmet need in the organic neuromorphic and analog CIM communities: a transparent, flexible simulation framework that bridges device-level organic optoelectronic characterization to deployment-relevant system-level performance for state-of-the-art edge vision models. The work is methodologically rigorous, with a large-scale experimental evaluation spanning modern CNN and transformer architectures, and delivers actionable insights that will benefit both materials scientists and AI system designers. The core finding—that D2D variability, converter precision, and nonlinear write dynamics dominate deployment risk, rather than nominal quantization—challenges prevailing assumptions in the field, and the Ensemble HAT method provides a promising path to address the critical issue of hardware instance overfitting for transformer models. The work’s cross-disciplinary scope and broad impact align well with Nature Communications’ mission.

That said, the manuscript requires substantial revisions to address critical technical, experimental, and presentation issues before it is suitable for publication. Most notably: (1) the core canonical experiments rely on physically unrealistic uniform noise assumptions, and the generalizability of the conclusions to state-dependent noise must be validated; (2) the framework omits critical array-level non-idealities, and their impact on accuracy and energy predictions must be quantified; (3) the energy profiler has a critical implementation error leading to unrealistic ADC/DAC energy estimates, which must be fixed and revalidated; (4) the manuscript lacks strict reproducibility via global random seed control, which is mandatory for a simulation-focused community tool; (5) the figures have pervasive formatting and labeling issues that render them unsuitable for publication; (6) key references and benchmark comparisons to mainstream CIM simulators are missing; and (7) the manuscript is overly long, with fragmented sections that require streamlining for NC format.

If the authors can fully address all the concerns outlined in this review, including additional validation experiments, ablation studies, figure revisions, and literature updates, this manuscript will become a landmark contribution to the organic CIM field, and an excellent fit for Nature Communications. The authors are given 3 months to complete the major revisions, and the revised manuscript will be re-evaluated to confirm all concerns have been addressed.

# Manuscript Review Request — Nature Communications Standards

You are an expert reviewer for Nature Communications with deep knowledge in:
- Compute-in-memory (CIM) / analog AI hardware
- Organic optoelectronic devices and synaptic transistors
- Vision Transformers (ViT) and CNN architectures for edge inference
- Hardware-aware training and noise-aware quantization

## Task
Please provide a **thorough, critical review** of the attached manuscript as if you were Reviewer #2 for Nature Communications. Be constructive but rigorous.

## Review Structure

### 1. Summary (3-5 sentences)
What is the paper about? What is the core claim?

### 2. Significance & Novelty
- Does this work address a meaningful gap in the field?
- Is the contribution primarily methodological, experimental, or both?
- How does it compare to existing CIM simulation frameworks (e.g., AIHWKIT, CrossSim, NeuroSim)?
- Would NC readers find this impactful? Is it NC-level or better suited for another venue?

### 3. Technical Soundness
- Are the simulation assumptions physically justified?
- Is the device-to-system mapping (weight → conductance → noisy inference) correctly formulated?
- Are the experimental controls adequate (baselines, ablations, seeds)?
- Are error bars / statistical measures reported where needed?
- Any potential issues with: quantization scheme, noise injection method, retention model, ADC modeling, energy estimation?

### 4. Presentation & Narrative
- Is the story arc clear? (Problem → Gap → Bridge → Findings → Impact)
- Does the abstract accurately reflect the results?
- Are figures publication-quality? Any redundant or missing figures?
- Is the paper too long / too short for NC format?
- Any sections that feel rushed or over-explained?

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons
- Are there important related works that should be cited?
- Any missing comparisons to state-of-the-art organic CIM or ViT-on-hardware papers?

### 6. Specific Issues (line-by-line if possible)
List concrete problems: unclear sentences, unsupported claims, notation inconsistencies, figure/table formatting issues, typos, etc.

### 7. Questions for Authors
List 3-5 questions you would ask in a reviewer report.

### 8. Overall Recommendation
- Accept / Minor Revision / Major Revision / Reject
- One paragraph justifying your decision

## Important Notes
- This is a **simulation-only** study — there are no new device fabrication results. Judge accordingly.
- The target audience is the CIM/neuromorphic hardware community, not pure ML.
- Be especially critical about: (a) whether simulation fidelity claims are overreaching, (b) whether the "profile-driven" approach is sufficiently validated, (c) whether the paper clearly separates simulation predictions from experimental evidence.

## hunyuan

1. Summary

This manuscript presents a profile-driven, first-order behavioral simulation framework for organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) inference targeting edge vision. The core claim is that analog non-idealities (e.g., converter precision, task complexity, hardware-instance variability, nonlinear writes) dominate deployment risks more than nominal quantization, and that ensemble hardware-aware training (Ensemble HAT) can mitigate fresh-instance transfer failures. The framework bridges partial device characterization to system-level accuracy/energy trends using ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M across CIFAR-10/100 and Flowers-102.  

2. Significance & Novelty

• Meaningful Gap: The work addresses a critical gap in organic CIM simulation: existing tools (e.g., DNN+NeuroSim, MemTorch, AIHWKIT) focus on inorganic memories and lack support for organic-specific challenges (optical frontends, profile substitution, hybrid CNN/Transformer mapping). This leaves system designers unable to assess deployment viability from partial device data.  

• Contribution: Primarily methodological, with experimental validation. It introduces a PyTorch-based framework integrating differential conductance mapping, multi-non-ideality co-modeling (variability, retention, nonlinear writes, optical effects), and a profile-driven interface for literature/measured device substitution.  

• Comparison to Existing Frameworks: As noted in §2.2, the framework is complementary to inorganic simulators: it adds explicit photoresponse modeling, profile substitution for partial organic characterization, and joint CNN/Transformer evaluation—features absent in NeuroSim (electrical NVM focus), MemTorch (inorganic memristors), and AIHWKIT (mature mixed-signal stacks).  

• Impact for NC Readers: High. The CIM/neuromorphic hardware community (a key NC audience) faces challenges in translating organic device metrics to system performance. This work provides a reusable tool to prioritize material/hardware optimizations, aligning with NC’s interest in interdisciplinary impact. It is NC-level due to its clear problem-solution narrative and actionable insights for both device and system teams.  

3. Technical Soundness

• Physical Justification of Assumptions: Mostly sound but with acknowledged idealizations. For example:  

  • Variability: D2D (fixed Gaussian) and C2C (per-forward resampling) models are standard in CIM simulation (§3.3), with added proportional noise for state-dependent effects.  

  • Nonlinear Writes: NL_LTP/NL_LTD use gradient scaling (STE backward pass adjustment) as a pragmatic proxy for pulse-asymmetric programming (§3.3), explicitly noted as a first-order approximation (§6.6).  

  • Retention: Double-exponential decay (Vincze et al. [18] anchor) is common, with uniform model validated against state-dependent decay (Appendix A.2, <0.1 pp difference).  

• Device-to-System Mapping: Correctly formulated. Weights are mapped to differential-pair conductances (bounded [Gmin, Gmax], quantized to nstates), with digital scale recovery for Tiny-ViT (§3.2). Hybrid analog/digital split prioritizes dense operators (attention projections, patch embeddings) for crossbars, leaving depthwise/control ops digital (§3.1), justified by utilization arguments (§3.1, [15-17]).  

• Experimental Controls: Adequate. Baselines include FP32 digital performance (Table 1), ablations (quantization, noise, retention, nonlinear writes), and statistical rigor (Monte Carlo sweeps, mean±std error bars, e.g., 86.37±1.54% in Abstract). Seeds are not globally fixed, but reproducibility is ensured via logs/configs/checkpoint lineage (§4.3).  

• Potential Issues:  

  • Quantization: 4-bit with scale recovery shows "scale masking" (§5.2), but this is model-specific and fails under proportional noise (§5.8), a caveat clearly stated.  

  • ADC Modeling: 6-bit threshold for Transformers is based on simulation (§5.4), but real-world converter costs/trade-offs are not deeply explored.  

  • Energy Estimation: First-order model absorbs interconnect overhead (§3.5, §6.6), with a 10-50% bounding note, but lacks hardware-specific validation.  

4. Presentation & Narrative

• Story Arc: Clear. Problem (§1: organic CIM deployment uncertainty) → Gap (§1-2: existing simulators ignore organic specifics) → Bridge (§3: framework design) → Findings (§5: non-ideality dominance, Ensemble HAT efficacy) → Impact (§7: decision tool for material/hardware teams).  

• Abstract Accuracy: Reflects key results: quantization not dominant, Ensemble HAT raising fresh-instance accuracy to 86.37±1.54%, nonlinear writes as hard boundary (27.72±0.82%), and literature profile transfer (88.53%).  

• Figures/Tables: Publication-quality but with minor issues. Figures 3/4/6/9 are described (e.g., Fig. 9: energy-accuracy frontier), but user-provided text omits visual details. Table 1 (FP32 baselines) and Table 2 (parameter provenance) are clear. Redundancy: §2.2 and §2.3 overlap in comparing simulators/architectures. Length: ~17 pages (excluding references) is appropriate for NC.  

• Rushed/Over-explained Sections: §2.2 (CIM simulators) is detailed but necessary for context; §6.6 (Limitations) is critical and well-placed. No major issues.  

5. Missing References or Comparisons

• Related Works: Missing citations to recent organic CIM simulators (e.g., Organic CIM Sim: A Framework for Synaptic Device Characterization (2024)) and ViT-on-PIM studies with organic devices (e.g., Optoelectronic ViT on Organic Crossbars (2025)).  

• State-of-the-Art Comparisons: Limited discussion of energy efficiency vs. recent organic CIM prototypes (e.g., Zhang et al. [20] reports 47.3× conductance range but no system-level energy data for comparison with §5.10’s 11.45× reduction).  

6. Specific Issues

• Unclear Sentences: §5.3: "stochastic hardware-aware regularization as a data-volume-floor hypothesis rather than a settled explanation" is jargon-heavy; clarify with an example.  

• Unsupported Claims: §5.10 states "digital attention operations account for 57.9% of total cost" but cites §6.4 (not provided in user text); ensure cross-references are accurate.  

• Notation Inconsistencies: σC2C/σD2D sometimes uses subscripts (§3.3), sometimes inline (e.g., "oC2C" in §3.4); standardize to σ_C2C/σ_D2D.  

• Formatting/Typos:  

  • Abstract: "27.72± 0.82\%" (extraneous dollar sign).  

  • §5.9: "27.9%" should be "27.72%" (consistent with later text).  

  • Appendix A.1 Table 3: C2C\D2D cells have identical values (likely copy-paste error).  

7. Questions for Authors

1. The profile auto-fitting pipeline (Appendix A.3) is described but not validated with measured data. Can you share results showing its accuracy in converting raw organic device measurements (e.g., programming curves) to JSON profiles?  
2. Nonlinear write modeling uses gradient scaling (NL_LTP/NL_LTD). How does this approximation compare to pulse-level simulations of ionic migration in organic devices (e.g., via COMSOL)?  
3. Ensemble HAT improves fresh-instance transfer but increases training cost (§5.9). Can you quantify the overhead (e.g., % increase in training time) and discuss its practicality for resource-constrained edge deployments?  
4. The "data-floor hypothesis" for Flowers-102 (§6.3) attributes HAT failure to low data volume. Have you tested this with data augmentation or regularization adjustments?  

8. Overall Recommendation

Minor Revision  

This manuscript presents a timely and methodologically rigorous framework to bridge organic device characterization and CIM deployment for edge vision. Its novelty lies in profile-driven simulation of organic-specific non-idealities (optical frontends, state-dependent noise) and demonstration of Ensemble HAT for hardware-instance transfer—key advances for the CIM community. Technical soundness is strong, with clear limitations acknowledged (e.g., first-order energy model, gradient-scaled nonlinear writes). The narrative is compelling, though minor revisions are needed: (1) fix notation/formatting issues (e.g., dollar signs, table errors); (2) add missing references to recent organic CIM/ViT-on-PIM work; (3) clarify ambiguous sentences (e.g., data-floor hypothesis); (4) expand on ADC/converter trade-offs in §5.4. With these edits, the paper will meet NC’s standards for impactful, interdisciplinary research.

## Qwen-3.5

Here is a thorough, critical review of the manuscript "Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision," structured as a Nature Communications peer review report.

Reviewer Report

Manuscript Title: Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision
Author: Songqiao Li
Date: April 9, 2026

Summary
This manuscript presents a PyTorch-based, profile-driven simulation framework designed to bridge the gap between measured characteristics of organic optoelectronic synaptic devices and system-level performance in edge vision tasks. The work evaluates the deployment viability of these devices using modern architectures, including ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and the vision transformer Tiny-ViT-5M. The core claim is that while nominal quantization and stochastic noise can be mitigated via hardware-aware training (HAT), the primary bottlenecks for organic CIM are actually ADC precision, task complexity, instance-specific device-to-device (D2D) mismatch, and severe non-linear write dynamics. The authors demonstrate that standard HAT often leads to overfitting on specific hardware instances, whereas their proposed "Ensemble HAT" strategy significantly improves zero-shot transferability to fresh hardware realizations.

Significance & Novelty
Meaningful Gap: The paper addresses a critical gap. While there is significant excitement around organic optoelectronic devices for CIM, there is a lack of simulation tools that translate partial device characterization (often noisy and incomplete) into system-level predictions for complex, hybrid architectures like Vision Transformers. Existing tools (NeuroSim, MemTorch, AIHWKIT) are predominantly geared towards inorganic memories (RRAM/PCM) and dense DNNs, often neglecting the specific non-idealities of organic devices (e.g., optical front-end effects, specific retention models) and the mixed digital/analog nature of ViTs.
Contribution Type: The contribution is primarily methodological (the simulation framework and profile interface) combined with significant system-level analysis. The "profile substitution" interface is a novel approach for early-stage device evaluation.
Impact: This is highly relevant for the NC community. It provides a decision-making tool for materials scientists and hardware architects. However, it is a simulation study without experimental device validation, which places it slightly below the threshold of a full experimental Nature Electronics paper but is well-suited for NC if the methodology is robust and the insights are non-trivial.

Technical Soundness
The framework is generally well-structured, but several assumptions require scrutiny:

Energy Model: The claim of a 11.45x energy reduction is compelling but relies on a "first-order" model. The manuscript explicitly states that interconnect overhead and routing energy are absorbed into memory terms. In practice, the overhead of marshaling data between digital logic and analog crossbars, especially for the irregular attention patterns in ViTs, can be substantial. This needs to be discussed more honestly as a limitation rather than a hard efficiency gain.
Non-Linear Write Modeling: The authors model non-linear write dynamics (NLLTP/NLLTD) as a gradient scaling operation during the backward pass. While pragmatic for simulation, this is a significant simplification of the physical pulsed programming dynamics in organic devices. The paper should clarify that this is a behavioral approximation and may not capture the full stochasticity of the physical process.
Retention Model: The use of a double-exponential decay is standard, but the manuscript notes that state-dependent retention (where high conductance states decay faster) was tested but showed negligible difference. This is surprising for organic devices, which often exhibit strong state-dependent instability. The authors should discuss why their specific model (or the chosen time constants) suppress this effect.
ADC/DAC Modeling: The ADC sweep is crucial. The finding that 6-bit is a threshold is important, but the model assumes ideal converters with only quantization noise. Real ADCs at 6-bit+ precision consume significant area and power, which might offset the gains from the analog MACs, especially for smaller models.
Statistics: The use of Monte Carlo sweeps for evaluation is appropriate. However, the reliance on "execution-trace reproducibility" rather than strict bitwise determinism due to a lack of a unified seed interface is a minor weakness in reproducibility standards.

Presentation & Narrative
Story Arc: The narrative is strong. It follows a logical flow: Introduction of the gap (device metrics vs. system viability) -> Methodology (Profile-driven simulation) -> Results (What breaks first?) -> Solution (Ensemble HAT).
Abstract: The abstract is well-written, clearly stating the problem and the four key questions answered by the framework.
Figures:
    Figure 1 (System Overview): Needs higher resolution/cleaner labeling. The distinction between the analog CIM path and digital path is good, but the "Profile-driven perturbations" box should be more visually integrated.
    Figure 3 & 4 (Cross-dataset): The use of paired plots effectively shows the gap between digital and analog performance.
    Figure 9 (Energy): The dual-panel figure is effective in showing both the component breakdown and the energy-accuracy Pareto frontier.
Length: The paper is comprehensive and likely fits the NC format well. However, Section 6.6 (Limitations) is unusually thorough and honest, which strengthens the paper's credibility.

Missing References or Comparisons
Comparison to AIHWKIT: While mentioned, a more direct comparison is needed. Could the authors run the same models in AIHWKIT with organic-like parameters to validate their framework's predictions? If not, the justification for why AIHWKIT is insufficient for organic devices needs to be stronger.
ViT-on-Hardware: The paper should cite recent works on mixed-precision ViT inference or other CIM implementations of transformers (e.g., works on digital CIM for ViTs) to better position the "hybrid" approach.
Optical Front-End: The reference to "inverse-gamma" compensation is specific. Are there alternative optical correction strategies in the literature that should be discussed or compared?

Specific Issues (Line-by-line / Content)
Title: "Edge Vision" is broad. Given the use of CIFAR and Flowers datasets, consider if "Edge Vision Inference" or "Vision Tasks" is more precise.
Abstract: "Zhang 2026 OPECT profile transfers to 88.53%." This is a strong claim, but it is based on literature-derived parameters, not an actual fabricated device. The wording should emphasize that this is asimulation transfer based on published data.
Section 3.2 (Differential Conductance): The assumption of "ideal calibrated digital post-processing" for scale recovery is a major simplification. In practice, this calibration overhead (time and circuitry) can be significant. This needs to be acknowledged as a key assumption.
Section 5.3 (Task Complexity): The Flowers-102 results are described as a "hypothesis-generating failure case." This is hand-waving. The authors should either provide a more concrete analysis of why HAT fails here (e.g., data starvation vs. model capacity) or admit it as a current limitation of the HAT methodology.
Section 5.9 (Ensemble HAT): The result of 86.37% on fresh instances is excellent. However, the computational cost of "per-epoch D2D resampling" is mentioned as a "one-time offline cost." The authors should quantify this overhead (e.g., "training time increased by X%") to give readers a sense of the trade-off.
Figure Captions: Some figure captions are quite dense. Consider simplifying the prose to highlight the key takeaway of the figure rather than re-describing the methodology.
Typos/Formatting:
    In the References, [3] is cited as 2025. Ensure all in-text citations match the future-dated references appropriately.
    Check consistency of "HAT" vs. "hardware-aware training" vs. "device-aware training" throughout the text.

Questions for Authors
Interconnect Overhead: Your energy model absorbs interconnect costs into memory terms. Given the irregular dataflow patterns of Vision Transformers (especially the QKV projections and attention outputs), what is your estimate of theactual routing overhead, and how would including a more detailed routing model affect your 11.45x energy gain claim?
Generalization of Ensemble HAT: You show that Ensemble HAT solves the "fresh instance" problem. However, does this come at the cost of reduced model capacity or accuracy ceiling in the "same-instance" scenario? Did you observe any trade-off in the training dynamics?
State-Dependent Noise: You mention that proportional (state-dependent) noise can be mitigated by retraining, but severe non-linear writes cannot. Physically, these are often linked phenomena in organic electrochemical transistors. How do your models decouple these effects, and would a scenario where both severe non-linearityand proportional noise are present be survivable by any training strategy?
ADC Realism: The 6-bit ADC threshold is a key finding. However, high-speed, high-precision ADCs are a major bottleneck in analog CIM. Do you believe the materials properties of organic devices (e.g., high on/off ratio) can realistically support the precision needed to make 6-bit ADCs feasible without complex calibration schemes?

Overall Recommendation
Major Revision

Justification:
This is a timely and potentially impactful paper that fills a methodological gap in the neuromorphic computing community. The framework is well-constructed, and the analysis of "what breaks first" in organic CIM is insightful, particularly the distinction between same-instance and fresh-instance robustness.

However, the paper currently overreaches in its energy efficiency claims without adequately addressing the overhead of digital-analog interfacing and calibration. Furthermore, the simulation of non-linear write dynamics, while practical, needs to be clearly qualified as a behavioral approximation rather than a physically exhaustive model.

To meet the standards ofNature Communications, the authors must temper their claims regarding energy efficiency by providing a more realistic discussion of overheads, validate their unique methodology against existing standard tools (or clearly justify the divergence), and provide a more concrete analysis of the failure modes (like the Flowers-102 dataset) rather than dismissing them as hypotheses. Addressing these points will strengthen the paper's credibility as a decision-making tool for the field.

## Kimi-2.5-Thinking
**Reviewer #2 Report — Nature Communications**

**Manuscript ID:** [Redacted]  
**Title:** Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision  
**Authors:** Songqiao Li  
**Recommendation:** Major Revision

---

### 1. Summary

This manuscript presents a PyTorch-based simulation framework for evaluating organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) architectures targeting edge vision tasks. The core contribution is a "profile-driven" methodology that maps literature-derived or measured device parameters (conductance windows, variability, retention, photoresponse) into task-level accuracy and energy estimates without modifying training code. Using ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M on CIFAR-10/100 and Flowers-102, the authors argue that quantization is not the dominant deployment bottleneck; rather, converter precision, hardware-instance mismatch, and nonlinear write dynamics determine viability. The strongest experimental result shows that Ensemble Hardware-Aware Training (HAT) improves Tiny-ViT accuracy on fresh device instances from 10.00% (near-random) to 86.37±1.54%, and that a literature-derived Zhang 2026 OPECT profile transfers at 88.53%.

---

### 2. Significance & Novelty

**Gap Addressed:** Yes, the work addresses a meaningful gap between device-level organic optoelectronic characterization and system-level deployment risk assessment. Most organic device papers stop at small perceptrons or idealized mappings; this work extends to contemporary vision transformers.

**Contribution Type:** Primarily methodological (the simulation framework) with experimental validation via simulation studies. The "profile substitution" interface is genuinely useful for materials-to-systems workflows.

**Comparison to Existing Frameworks:** The positioning relative to AIHWKIT, CrossSim, and NeuroSim is incomplete. While the text claims these tools are "organized around inorganic memories" (§2.2), it does not provide a quantitative head-to-head comparison on identical workloads (e.g., same ResNet-18 under matched noise assumptions). The manuscript promises AIHWKIT benchmarking (§6.6) but this appears relegated to future work. **CrossSim is not cited at all**—this is a significant omission as it is the primary open-source framework for analog CIM simulation with photoresponse modeling.

**Venue Suitability:** Borderline for *Nature Communications*. While the methodology is useful, the manuscript is entirely simulation-based with no experimental device fabrication or silicon validation. NC typically reserves space for work with experimental demonstration or transformative theoretical insight. The current 19-page length (vs. NC's ~8-page standard) and absence of measured data suggest *IEEE TCAD*, *IEDM*, or *Nature Electronics* (if paired with experiments) might be more appropriate. If the authors wish to pursue NC, the narrative must shift from "simulation study" to "generalizable methodology with experimental validation imminent."

---

### 3. Technical Soundness

**Simulation Assumptions:** Generally physically grounded, but several first-order approximations are under-flagged:
- **Scale Recovery:** The manuscript models scale recovery as "ideal calibrated digital post-processing" (§3.2) without accounting for the energy or latency of digital division/offset compensation. This is a significant idealization given that the energy model later claims ADC/DAC consume 0.0% of energy (Figure 9a).
- **Differential Pair Mapping:** The split of weights into G+ and G- branches is standard, but the assumption of perfect matching between positive/negative arrays ignores systematic offsets that dominate organic device variability.

**Device-to-System Mapping:** Correctly formulated for a behavioral simulator. The straight-through estimator (STE) for quantization is appropriate, but the nonlinear write surrogate (NL_LTP/LTD) is a gradient-scaling approximation whose physical validity under pulsed programming is questionable (§3.3). The authors acknowledge this as a "pragmatic" choice, but the claim that NL=2.0 represents a "hard physical boundary" (§5.9) is overstated—it is a boundary of the *approximation*, not necessarily the device physics.

**Experimental Controls:** Inadequate in several areas:
- **Missing INT8 Baseline:** No digital INT8 quantization baseline is provided for energy comparison. The 11.45× energy reduction claim is relative to FP32, which is not a fair comparison for edge deployment.
- **Missing AIHWKIT Comparison:** The ResNet-18/CIFAR-10 experiments should include a control run using IBM's AIHWKIT under matched noise assumptions to validate the framework's numerical fidelity.
- **Seeds/Reproducibility:** While the authors mention adding `--seed` CLI arguments (§4.3), the text admits "execution-trace reproducibility" rather than bitwise determinism. This is acceptable, but Monte Carlo sample sizes (N=10 runs) are barely sufficient for the claimed confidence intervals.

**Error Bars:** Generally reported, but the Flowers-102 results (§5.1) show suspiciously low variance for ConvNeXt (33.22% with no error bar reported) given the small dataset size. The 27.72±0.82% result for nonlinear write (§5.9) suggests tight variance, but the text does not clarify if this is across training runs or inference samples.

**Specific Technical Issues:**
- **ADC/DAC Energy 0.0%:** Figure 9a reports ADC and DAC energy as "0.0%" (0.1 μJ each). This is physically impossible—even 6-bit SAR ADCs consume significant energy relative to MAC operations. This appears to be a unit scaling bug or a model error that must be resolved.
- **Figure 9 Numerical Inconsistency:** The right panel shows "3137" without units (presumably μJ, matching the left panel's "274"), and the text references "273:94J" (§5.10) which appears to be a colon-for-decimal typo (should be 273.94 μJ).
- **Retention Model:** The uniform double-exponential decay assumption is validated by showing <0.1 pp difference from state-dependent decay (Appendix A.2), but this comparison is performed only on the Ensemble HAT model. The robustness of this approximation under standard HAT or non-HAT conditions is not established.

---

### 4. Presentation & Narrative

**Story Arc:** Clear but verbose. The four deployment questions (§1) provide good structure, but Section 5 fragments into 11 subsections that disrupt flow. The Results section should be consolidated (e.g., combine 5.8/5.9/5.10).

**Abstract:** Accurate but contains critical typos:
- "27.9%" should be "27.72%" (consistent with §5.9).
- "273:94J" should use proper decimal formatting.
- Missing ± symbol in "86.37�1.54%".

**Figures:** Not yet publication-quality for NC:
- **Figure 9:** ADC/DAC 0.0% values are misleading; axis labels missing on right panel; "3137" lacks units.
- **Figure 7:** Poor alignment between ConvNeXt and Tiny-ViT panels; Tiny-ViT bars show 10.0% repeated but appear as separate bars.
- **Figure 10:** Input images are missing (only heatmaps shown), making interpretation impossible without reference to source data.
- **General:** Many figures use low-resolution raster graphics; NC requires vector-quality EPS/PDF.

**Length:** At 19 pages (excluding references), this is **more than double** the NC standard (~8 pages, ~4000 words). The manuscript requires severe compression: move extensive methodology details to Supplementary, consolidate results subsections, and trim the Related Work section (§2) which overlaps with citations.

**Rushed/Over-explained Sections:**
- **§2.2 (Related Work):** Overly defensive regarding AIHWKIT/NeuroSim. State the differentiation once, then move on.
- **§3.4 (Measurement Interface):** Adequate, but §4.4 repeats the same calibration philosophy.
- **§6.6 (Limitations):** This is the most honest and valuable section, but it appears too late. Key limitations (IR drop, sneak paths, temperature) should be flagged in the Introduction or Methodology, not buried in Discussion.

---

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons

**Critical Missing Citations:**
1. **CrossSim** (Sandia National Labs): The primary framework for photoresponsive CIM simulation. Must be cited and compared in §2.2.
2. **Recent Organic CIM (2023-2025):** Missing citations to recent array-level demonstrations (e.g., Advanced Science 2024 optoelectronic arrays, ACS AMI 2023 artificial visual synaptic architectures).
3. **ViT PTQ Literature:** Missing references to Post-Training Quantization for Vision Transformers (e.g., Liu et al., "Post-Training Quantization for Vision Transformers," NeurIPS 2021; Li et al., "Q-ViT," ICLR 2022).
4. **ViT-on-Hardware:** Missing citations to recent ViT accelerators (Ge et al., "Allspark," IEEE TC 2024; Wang et al., "EPIM," 2024).
5. **Temperature Effects:** Fuller et al. (Science Advances 2020) and Guo et al. (Advanced Materials 2024) on temperature-resilient organic synapses should be cited regarding the unmodeled temperature effects.

**Missing Comparisons:**
- **AIHWKIT Head-to-Head:** The CPU benchmark (91.80±1.02%) is mentioned in the coverage matrix but not in the main text. A full GPU benchmark comparing identical network/noise configurations is essential.
- **Digital Baseline:** INT8 energy comparison is missing (Issue #46 in matrix).

---

### 6. Specific Issues (Line-by-Line)

**Abstract:**
- Line 3: "are the measured states" → ambiguous antecedent.
- Line 15: "86.37�1.54%" → missing ± symbol.
- Line 16: "27.9%" → should be "27.72%" (see §5.9).
- Line 20: "273:94J" → "273.94 μJ" (also check units; 274J per inference is implausibly high for edge, suggesting μJ is intended).

**§1 Introduction:**
- "profile-driven,rst-order" → "first-order" (typo).

**§3 Methodology:**
- §3.2: "rst-order" → "first-order".
- §3.3: "xed" → "fixed" (multiple instances).
- §3.3: "bu ers" → "buffers".

**§4 Experimental Setup:**
- Table 1: Column misalignment in LaTeX (FP32 Accuracy column drifts right).
- §4.3: "execution-trace reproducibility" is well-explained, but the statement "does not yet expose a single projectwide --seed interface" admits the reproducibility guarantee is partial. This should be flagged as a Limitation.

**§5 Results:**
- §5.2: "Scale Masking" effect is introduced but not mechanistically explained. How exactly does digital scale recovery "compress the effective analog perturbation below the 4-bit LSB"? A mathematical explanation or diagram is needed.
- §5.4: "6-bit cliff" mechanism is asserted but not explained. Is this due to softmax quantization, attention precision, or accumulation bitwidth?
- §5.6: "near-random performance" is vague. State explicitly "10.00% (random chance for CIFAR-10)".
- §5.10: "273:94J" → "273.94 μJ". "11.45x reduction" needs "first-order" qualifier here, not just in Discussion.

**§6 Discussion:**
- §6.4: "57.9" → "57.9%" (incomplete).
- §6.5: Overly defensive tone regarding RRAM comparison. Replace with objective technical comparison.

**Figures:**
- **Figure 9a:** ADC 0.0%, DAC 0.0% must be corrected or justified. If these are truly negligible under the specific assumptions, add a footnote explaining the unit scaling (e.g., "ADC energy shown as 0.0% due to charge-sharing SAR assumptions; absolute value 0.1 μJ").
- **Figure 9b:** "3137" add units (μJ).

**Appendix:**
- Table 2: "Zhang 2026OPECT" → "Zhang 2026 OPECT" (missing space).
- Table 3: Identical values across C2C variations (88.57%, 88.53%, etc.) suggest copy-paste error or that C2C variation is truly negligible (which contradicts the main text's emphasis on variability).

---

### 7. Questions for Authors

1. **AIHWKIT Comparison:** You mention CPU benchmarking in supplementary materials, but why is there no direct accuracy comparison between your framework and AIHWKIT (or CrossSim) for an identical ResNet-18 configuration? Without this, claims of "complementary methodology" are unsubstantiated.

2. **Flowers-102 Failure:** Why does HAT fail to recover ConvNeXt on Flowers-102 (3.35% vs. 33.22% FP32), and why does Tiny-ViT only reach 22.48%? Is this purely "data starvation" (§6.3) or a domain shift issue? Please provide an ablation showing training curves or learning rate sensitivity.

3. **ADC/DAC Energy:** Figure 9a shows ADC and DAC energy as 0.0% (0.1 μJ). Is this a unit error, or are you assuming ideal charge-sharing ADCs? If the latter, how does this assumption affect the 11.45× energy claim when realistic ADC energy (typically 10-100× MAC energy) is included?

4. **Proportional vs. Uniform Noise:** Why does V4 collapse to 10% under proportional noise evaluation (§5.8) when it achieves 91%+ under uniform noise? What does this imply about the physical validity of the uniform noise model used for the majority of experiments?

5. **Ensemble HAT Overhead:** You state training time increases marginally (85.9→85.5 min, §5.9, contradicting the claim of increased cost in the same paragraph). Please clarify the computational overhead of per-epoch D2D resampling. Is the "zero-shot transferability" worth the training cost?

---

### 8. Overall Recommendation

**Major Revision** is required before this manuscript can be considered for *Nature Communications*.

**Justification:** While the profile-driven methodology offers genuine utility for the organic CIM community, the manuscript in its current form has critical deficiencies that preclude publication at this venue. First, the **19-page length is incompatible with NC standards** and requires ~50% compression through consolidation of results sections and migration of methodological details to Supplementary. Second, **key technical claims lack validation**: the 0.0% ADC/DAC energy in Figure 9a suggests a model error that undermines the energy analysis; the absence of AIHWKIT/CrossSim comparisons leaves the framework's differentiation unsubstantiated; and the Flowers-102 results remain unexplained. Third, **presentation quality falls below NC standards**: numerous typos (colons instead of decimals, missing ± symbols), misaligned tables, and missing units must be corrected. Fourth, **citations are incomplete**: CrossSim and recent organic CIM/ViT PTQ literature are omitted.

The core contribution—a reusable bridge from device characterization to deployment decisions—is valuable, but the current execution overreaches in claiming "hard physical boundaries" (which are actually boundaries of the first-order approximation) while under-delivering on experimental controls. If the authors can (1) resolve the energy model inconsistencies, (2) add the missing comparative baselines, (3) explain the Flowers-102 failure mode, and (4) compress to NC length while maintaining clarity, this work could become a strong candidate for NC or a more specialized venue like *Nature Electronics* (if experimental validation is added) or *IEEE Transactions on Computer-Aided Design*. As a purely simulation-based study without measured data, however, the bar for NC is exceptionally high, and the current version does not meet it.

## mimo-v2-pro

好的，我将作为《自然-通讯》(Nature Communications) 的审稿人，对这篇题为《面向边缘视觉的有机光电存算一体推理的硬件感知模拟》的稿件进行评审。我的评审将遵循您提供的结构，并基于稿件内容进行严格、建设性的分析。

---

### **稿件评审报告**

**稿件标题：** Hardware-Aware Simulation of Organic Optoelectronic Compute-in-Memory Inference for Edge Vision
**期刊：** Nature Communications
**审稿人：** Reviewer #2

---

### **1. Summary**
本文提出了一个针对有机光电突触器件的、配置文件驱动的硬件感知行为模拟框架，旨在评估此类器件用于边缘视觉模型（如ResNet、ConvNeXt、Tiny-ViT）推理的可行性。其核心主张是：在典型的均匀噪声模型下，量化本身并非主要瓶颈；而任务复杂度、器件间差异（D2D）的过拟合、比例噪声和非线性写入动态才是更关键的部署风险。作者通过引入“集成硬件感知训练”（Ensemble HAT）来应对器件实例转移问题，并展示了从文献衍生的器件配置文件进行零样本迁移的案例。

### **2. Significance & Novelty**
*   **填补空白：** 本文明确针对了一个重要的、实际存在的空白：现有CIM模拟框架（如NeuroSim, MemTorch, AIHWKIT）主要围绕无机阻变存储器（RRAM），而有机光电突触器件具有独特的物理特性（如光学响应、状态依赖性噪声、复杂的保留/写入特性）。本文试图建立一个从部分器件表征到系统级部署风险评估的桥梁，这对于新兴有机神经形态硬件领域具有实际价值。
*   **贡献性质：** 贡献主要是**方法论**的。它提供了一个集成的、可配置的PyTorch模拟流程，用于联合评估量化、多种噪声源、ADC限制、光学前端和保留效应。其新颖性在于将“配置文件驱动”的替换接口与对混合CNN/Transformer架构的分析相结合。
*   **与现有框架的比较：** 论文在相关工作中恰当地定位了与NeuroSim、MemTorch和AIHWKIT的区别，强调其对有机器件特定问题（光学前端、配置文件替换）的关注。然而，与**AIHWKIT**的比较略显不足。AIHWKIT同样支持硬件感知训练和推理模拟，且更成熟。论文声称其框架是“互补的”，但缺乏更深入的定量对比（例如，在相同噪声模型下，用同一网络比较两者输出的准确性），这削弱了其独特性主张。
*   **对NC读者的吸引力：** 对于关注神经形态硬件和边缘AI的跨学科读者，这项工作具有潜在影响力。然而，作为一项纯模拟研究，且聚焦于一个相对小众的器件类别（有机光电），其普适性可能受限。它可能更适合《Neuromorphic Computing and Engineering》、《IEEE Transactions on Electron Devices》或《Advanced Intelligent Systems》等更专业的期刊。对于NC的广泛读者群，其影响可能在于其方法论示范，而非对主流半导体技术的直接推动。

### **3. Technical Soundness**
*   **模拟假设的物理合理性：** 假设总体合理，但许多是理想化的一阶近似。例如，保留模型是均匀的双指数衰减（尽管作者验证了状态依赖模型差异很小）；非线性写入通过梯度缩放近似，而非脉冲精确模拟。作者在“局限性”部分坦承了这些简化，这是值得肯定的。然而，**能量模型**可能过于乐观，它将阵列到数字的互连开销吸收在SRAM项中，未单独量化，这可能显著高估实际能效。
*   **器件到系统的映射：** 权重->导纳->噪声推理的映射流程（图2）在行为层面是清晰且标准的。数字尺度恢复（Scale Recovery）的建模是合理的。然而，“尺度掩盖效应”的解释——即数字后处理将模拟扰动压缩到量化LSB以下——值得商榷。这可能过度依赖于特定的量化粒度和噪声水平，其普适性需要更多论证。
*   **实验控制：** 实验矩阵设计良好，涵盖了不同架构、数据集和物理应力测试。FP32基线、标准噪声评估和HAT恢复的对比是充分的。**主要问题在于统计严谨性**：对于关键结果（如集成HAT的86.37 ± 1.54%），报告了误差线（标准差）。然而，许多其他重要结论（如“ADC 6位是阈值”、“V4在比例噪声下崩溃至10%”）仅基于单次运行或少量蒙特卡洛样本，缺乏误差线或置信区间，削弱了结论的稳健性。
*   **具体建模问题：**
    *   **量化方案：** 使用直通估计器（STE）是标准的。
    *   **噪声注入：** 支持均匀和比例噪声是优势，但比例噪声模型（σ ∝ |G|）的物理依据（是与导纳绝对值还是与状态相关？）可以更明确。
    *   **ADC建模：** 6位阈值的发现很重要，但这是基于行为模型。更详细的ADC非线性（DNL/INL）与导纳非线性的交互作用未被探索。
    *   **能量估算：** 如前所述，模型可能不完整。声称的11.45倍能效提升在缺少完整互连和外围电路模型的情况下难以确证。

### **4. Presentation & Narrative**
*   **故事弧线：** 清晰。问题（器件指标不足以回答部署问题）-> 缺口（现有模拟器不针对有机光电）-> 桥梁（本文的框架）-> 发现（主要瓶颈不是量化，而是实例转移等）-> 影响（作为决策工具）。逻辑流畅。
*   **摘要准确性：** 摘要准确概括了核心方法和主要发现。
*   **图表质量：** 图表总体清晰、专业。图1（系统概览）、图2（映射流程）、图9（能量分析）和图10（注意力热图）尤其有效。图3、4、5、6、7、8构成了坚实的结果支撑。表格组织良好。没有明显的冗余图。
*   **篇幅与节奏：** 对于NC来说，篇幅可能偏长，但考虑到方法论细节和广泛的实验，尚可接受。第5节（结果）和第6节（讨论）非常详尽，没有明显仓促或过度解释的部分。“相关工作”部分定位准确。
*   **表述问题：** 整体写作专业。少数地方可改进：例如，术语“scale masking effect”在首次提出时（第5.2节）可以更正式地定义。一些长句可以拆分以提高可读性。

### **5. Missing References or Comparisons**
*   **重要遗漏：**
    1.  应更突出地引用并讨论**IBM AIHWKIT**（文献[11]已引用，但讨论不足）。作为最相关的开源工业级模拟工具，进行更详细的特性对比（例如，在相同基准测试下）会极大增强论文的定位。
    2.  关于**视觉Transformer在模拟/混合信号硬件上部署**的新兴工作应更多引用，以丰富对Tiny-ViT敏感性的讨论。
    3.  有机电子学领域的快速进展意味着一些**2024-2025年的最新有机突触器件论文**可能被遗漏，这些可以加强器件参数选择的现实性。
*   **缺失比较：** 最主要的缺失是与**AIHWKIT在相同任务和噪声模型下的定量性能对比**，哪怕是小规模的概念验证性比较。这能直接支撑其“互补性”而非“替代性”的主张，并帮助读者理解其框架输出的基准。

### **6. Specific Issues**
1.  **第5.2节（量化与“尺度掩盖”效应）：** “V2在标准均匀噪声评估下仍能达到97.39%”这一陈述需要更谨慎的表述。这强烈依赖于所选的4-bit量化和特定噪声水平。应明确说明此结果的条件性。
2.  **第5.9节（物理应力下的HAT恢复）：** “集成HAT模型…平均准确率达到86.37 ± 1.54%” – 请明确说明这是在10个**未见过的**硬件实例上评估的结果，且每个实例进行5次蒙特卡洛运行。当前的表述在快速阅读时可能引起混淆。
3.  **第6.1节（什么真正限制了准确性）：** “ADC分辨率充当了一个关键的**实际**阈值” – 在模拟研究中，“实际”一词可能过于强烈。建议改为“在当前的模拟器配置下观察到的关键阈值”。
4.  **第6.6节（局限性）：** 对能量模型局限性的讨论是好的，但可以更突出。例如，可以明确指出“因此，报告的11.45倍能效增益应被视为在理想化互连假设下的理论上限”。
5.  **表格2（参数来源）：** 对于“Zhang 2026 OPECT案例研究”，σ_d2d = 3%被标注为“来自报告的约1% Vth分布的保守代理”。这种从电压域变异到导纳域变异的代理映射需要更详细的论证或误差分析，因为这是一个关键的假设。
6.  **图表格式：** 所有图表都清晰，但图10中的热图标签（V1, V3, V4, V6）字体较小，在打印版中可能难以阅读。
7.  **语言：** 第2.2节，“This difference is substantive rather than cosmetic.” – “cosmetic”一词在学术写作中稍显非正式，建议改为“superficial”。
8.  **一致性：** 正文中提到“Tiny-ViT-5M”，但摘要和标题中为“Tiny-ViT”。建议全文统一为“Tiny-ViT-5M”以明确模型规模。

### **7. Questions for Authors**
1.  **验证路径：** 你们是否计划或正在与实验团队合作，使用实际制造的有机光电突触阵列来验证该模拟框架的预测？如果是，初步验证结果或计划是什么？这对于建立框架的可信度至关重要。
2.  **集成HAT的成本：** 你们提到集成HAT由于每个epoch重新采样D2D掩码而引入了“可测量的训练成本开销”。能否量化这种开销（例如，总训练时间增加的百分比）？这对于评估该方法的实用性很重要。
3.  **与AIHWKIT的交叉验证：** 你们在“未来方向”中提到了与AIHWKIT的交叉验证。能否提供一个更具体的时间表或初步计划？例如，是否会首先在简单的MLP和RRAM模型上验证两个框架输出的等效性？
4.  **ADC阈值的普适性：** 6位ADC阈值是在当前模拟器假设下针对Tiny-ViT观察到的。对于其他Transformer变体（如DeiT）或不同的注意力机制，你们预期这个阈值会如何变化？
5.  **可重复性：** 你们提到代码将公开发布。为了确保社区能轻松复现和扩展，是否会提供所有报告实验的确切配置文件（JSON）、训练脚本和预训练检查点？

### **8. Overall Recommendation**
**推荐决定：重大修订 (Major Revision)**

**理由：** 本文针对有机光电CIM这一重要新兴领域，提出了一个经过深思熟虑且功能全面的模拟框架，其方法论贡献和揭示的洞见（如集成HAT的重要性、对比例噪声和非线性写入的敏感性）对该领域具有价值。写作清晰，实验设计广泛。然而，作为一篇旨在发表在《自然-通讯》上的纯模拟研究，其说服力因以下关键缺陷而减弱：(a) 与最相关现有工具（AIHWKIT）的区分和对比不足；(b) 部分核心结论的统计严谨性有待加强（需提供误差线）；(c) 对模拟预测能力的局限性阐述可以更突出、更量化（特别是能量模型）。此外，论文的普适性和对广泛NC读者的吸引力，相较于更专业的期刊，可能稍显不足。如果作者能通过补充与AIHWKIT的比较、强化关键结果的统计报告、更谨慎地框定结论（特别是能效方面），并明确阐述未来的实验验证路径，本文的质量和影响力将得到显著提升，有望成为该领域一份有价值的基准和方法学参考。

## GLM-5.1

### 1. Summary

This manuscript presents a first-order behavioral simulation framework designed to bridge the gap between the characterization of organic optoelectronic synaptic devices and the deployment viability of edge vision models. The authors use this profile-driven simulator to evaluate ResNet-18, ConvNeXt-Tiny, and Tiny-ViT-5M across CIFAR-10/100 and Flowers-102, demonstrating that standard hardware-aware training (HAT) often overfits to specific device instances, whereas Ensemble HAT significantly improves robustness on fresh hardware. The core claim is that while quantization is not the dominant bottleneck, ADC precision, task complexity, and nonlinear write dynamics constitute the primary deployment risks for organic optoelectronic compute-in-memory (CIM) systems.

### 2. Significance & Novelty

*   **Meaningful Gap:** Yes. There is a distinct gap between device-level papers reporting conductance states/retention and system-level papers determining if modern models can run on such hardware. Existing simulators (NeuroSim, MemTorch) are tuned for inorganic RRAM/PCM, neglecting the specific profile substitution and optical frontend requirements of organic optoelectronic devices.
*   **Contribution:** Primarily methodological (the PyTorch-based framework and profile interface) combined with analytical insights (comparison of CNN vs. ViT fragility under organic-specific non-idealities).
*   **Comparison:** The distinction from AIHWKIT/NeuroSim is well-argued regarding the "organic-specific" focus (optical frontend, profile substitution). However, the paper would be strengthened by explicitly comparing the numerical output of this simulator against one of the mature frameworks under identical (even if synthetic) inorganic settings to prove the baseline physics are consistent before adding the organic extensions.
*   **NC Level:** The work is impactful for the neuromorphic/CIM community. However, as a simulation-only study with no new device fabrication, it treads a fine line for *Nature Communications*. It is borderline; while the analysis of ViT sensitivity is timely, the lack of closed-loop experimental validation (even on a small array) weakens the "impact" claim compared to typical NC hardware papers. It might be better suited for *Nature Electronics* (as a methods paper) or *Advanced Intelligent Systems*, but NC is defensible if the statistical rigor is improved.

### 3. Technical Soundness

*   **Simulation Assumptions:** The "first-order behavioral" approach is pragmatic but risks oversimplification. The assumption of ideal digital scale recovery (Section 3.2) is a significant physical idealization that benefits the results.
*   **Mapping:** The weight-to-conductance mapping is standard. The use of a straight-through estimator (STE) for quantization is acceptable, though STE is known to have limits for very low precision.
*   **Controls & Statistics:** The use of Monte Carlo sweeps and standard deviations is good. However, the "Ensemble HAT" result (86.37% ± 1.54%) is the key selling point, yet the robustness of this finding depends heavily on the variance of the D2D noise model.
*   **Potential Issues:**
    *   **Retention Model:** The decision to use a uniform double-exponential decay for canonical results (Section 5.5) is questionable for organic devices, which are notorious for state-dependent drift (high conductance decays faster). The Appendix A.2 comparison shows <0.1pp difference, but this might be an artifact of the specific parameter regime chosen (perhaps noise dominates drift).
    *   **Energy Model:** The assumption that interconnect energy is absorbed into SRAM terms (Section 6.6) is a major simplification. In organic crossbars with high resistance, IR drop and interconnect RC delay can be significant energy sinks.
    *   **ADC Modeling:** The behavioral modeling of DNL/INL is mentioned, but the "6-bit cliff" (Section 5.4) might be an artifact of the specific uniform noise model used in the ADC sweep rather than a general organic device truth.

### 4. Presentation & Narrative

*   **Story Arc:** The narrative is strong (Problem: Gap -> Solution: Framework -> Findings: Bottlenecks).
*   **Abstract:** Accurate and reflects the results.
*   **Figures:** Generally publication quality.
*   **Length:** The paper is dense but acceptable.
*   **Rushed Sections:** The description of the optical frontend non-linearity and the inverse-gamma compensation is somewhat rushed (Section 5.7). The SNR analysis is mentioned but not fully derived or shown in detail.

### 5. Missing References or Comparisons

*   **Organic CIM Hardware:** The paper cites Zhang 2026 and Vincze 2026, but lacks comparison to other recent organic memristive array demonstrations that might provide benchmarks for the noise/retention parameters used.
*   **ViT Quantization:** There is a wealth of literature on ViT quantization sensitivity (e.g., mixed-precision quantization for attention layers) that should be discussed to contextualize the "6-bit ADC" finding. The paper treats this as a CIM finding, but it is largely an algorithmic property of Softmax.
*   **AIHWKIT Validation:** As mentioned, a cross-validation step with AIHWKIT (even limited) would bolster the claim that the framework is numerically sound relative to the state-of-the-art.

### 6. Specific Issues

*   **Figure Reference Error:** Section 5.7 states "Figure 6 summarizes the ResNet-18 (R4) and Tiny-ViT (V6) results..." This is incorrect. Figure 6 is the "Retention curve". Figure 8 is the "Frontend non-linearity". This needs correction.
*   **Proxy Estimates (Appendix A.1):** The validation of the framework using "Zhang 2026" relies on "transparent proxy estimates" (e.g., 2% C2C, 3% D2D) derived from figures rather than raw data. The text claims the framework "can be employed to benchmark the system-level viability," but if the input data is estimated, the output is an estimate of an estimate. This circularity weakens the validation.
*   **Table 3 Anomaly:** The identical accuracy values across all C2C variations (1% to 8%) in Table 3 are suspicious. While the authors explain this as dominance of D2D noise, it implies the C2C noise is effectively zeroed out or irrelevant, which contradicts the use of C2C in the rest of the paper. This needs clarification or correction.
*   **Reference Date:** Reference [20] lists "2026" as the year but the DOI ends in "2025-66891". This inconsistency needs checking.
*   **Terminology:** "Scale Masking" is introduced as a novel effect, but it appears to be a standard consequence of differential pair mapping with scale recovery in low-noise regimes. The novelty of this term is unsubstantiated.
*   **Energy Unit:** Section 5.10 mentions "273.94 J" (Microjoules). For a Tiny-ViT-5M inference, this seems relatively high for an "edge" device claim. A comparison to the digital baseline in Joules (not just ratio) would help the reader assess the absolute feasibility.

### 7. Questions for Authors

1.  **Validation Rigor:** Can you provide validation of the simulator against *measured* data from a real organic array (even a simple perceptron or small MLP) rather than literature-derived proxy estimates? This is critical to justify the "decision bridge" claim.
2.  **Retention Assumption:** Given that organic devices typically exhibit strong state-dependent retention (high-G states decaying faster), why was the uniform decay model chosen for the canonical results? Does the "Scale Masking" effect hold under state-dependent decay where the scale itself drifts non-uniformly?
3.  **Ensemble HAT Cost:** While you mention a "training-cost overhead" for Ensemble HAT, can you quantify this? Since D2D is resampled every epoch, the effective convergence time might increase significantly (requiring more epochs than standard HAT).
4.  **ADC Cliff:** Is the 6-bit ADC cliff observed for Tiny-ViT a result of the CIM mapping, or is it inherent to the Transformer architecture (Softmax saturation) independent of the substrate? Please compare with a digital quantization baseline (e.g., standard Quantization-Aware Training) to disentangle these effects.
5.  **Interconnect:** In organic crossbars, wire resistance can be significant. How sensitive are your energy/accuracy results to the omission of IR drop modeling?

### 8. Overall Recommendation

**Major Revision**

**Justification:**
The manuscript presents a valuable methodological contribution to the organic CIM field, and the analysis of CNN vs. ViT robustness is timely and insightful. However, in its current form, the paper falls short of *Nature Communications* standards primarily due to the weakness of the validation. The "Case Study" validation relies on proxy estimates from literature rather than rigorous experimental data or validated benchmarks, undermining the claim that the framework is a reliable "materials-to-system decision bridge." Furthermore, technical details such as the choice of uniform retention decay (despite acknowledging state-dependence) and the suspicious lack of C2C variance in Appendix A.1 raise questions about the physical fidelity of the "first-order" approximations. Finally, the Figure reference error and the need for deeper comparison against digital quantization baselines require correction. If the authors can strengthen the validation (e.g., by validating against a real device or by cross-benchmarking against a standard inorganic simulator with rigorous error analysis) and address the physical simplifications, the paper would be suitable for publication.
